Page 5

United States Stops Buying Silver; London Silver Market Stalls; 20 Million Ounces Dumped; Silver Prices Plummet and Cannot Be Quoted; Recent Situation Heard to Have Improved Slightly

(London) As a result of the disastrous drop in world silver prices, London silver brokers have suspended trading for one day today. Sellers were seven times more than usual, mostly from the East, because of the belief that the United States has changed its silver purchase policy. The market dumped a huge amount of silver, from 18 million to 20 million ounces, and no one asked about it. Silver prices could not be quoted, the first time since the European War in 1914. The silver price was originally scheduled to be quoted at 4:15 PM, but since no one was buying, trading was temporarily suspended. However, the situation should be slightly clearer tomorrow. (10th National Telegram)

(New York) Affected by the suspension of the London silver market, the silver price here today was delayed for a long time. The final price was set at 63 and 3/4 cents per ounce, down one cent from yesterday. (10th National Telegram)

(London) After yesterday's disturbances, the London silver market has been less panic-stricken today. Far Eastern and Indian speculators are naturally facing difficulties given recent developments. Therefore, the number of sales today is not as large as yesterday. Many clients are selling at limit prices. People in the silver market now hold hope that spot prices can be quoted. As for forward prices, it may be difficult to settle for the time being. It is expected that spot prices can be settled at around 28 pence. The attitude of the United States has not yet been clarified. At the same time, foreign exchange rates are now feeling the reverberations of the silver market turmoil. The price of the pound sterling, converted to US dollars and gold pounds, is weaker, because there is fear that the US dollar will lack the stability if the US does not buy silver as before. Gold has benefited from the increase in the price of the US dollar. (11th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Because the United States did not entrust purchases, the silver market could not be quoted and priced today, which is unprecedented in the London silver market, resulting in complete chaos in the market. In the past, around 2:00 PM, brokers would determine the price based on all sales and purchases, but when brokers gathered as usual today, they saw only sales and no purchase entrustments. Therefore, it was decided to temporarily suspend trading, hoping that the US Treasury Department would re-enter the market and absorb as much of the sales as possible. However, when trading resumed, the US Treasury Department was only prepared to purchase a small amount of silver at a lower price than yesterday, only one-seventh of the total sales. According to exchange regulations, all sales must be completely absorbed at the settled price. Therefore, the brokers had no choice but to be unable to settle the price. It is heard that the United States is willing to purchase 2 million ounces at a price of 28.375 pence, 0.375 pence lower than yesterday, while the sales orders received by the brokers totaled 5 million ounces. According to reliable news outside the silver market, most of the sales were for forward transactions, about 12 million ounces, while there were very few buyers of forward transactions. (10th Reuters)

Statement from the US Treasury Department Denies Abandoning the Silver Purchase Act

(Washington) A spokesperson for US Treasury Secretary Morgenthau criticized the collapse of the London silver market today and denied that the US Treasury Department had abandoned the provisions of the Silver Purchase Act. Morgenthau is not in Washington, but the situation in the silver market has been reported to him in detail. According to the opinion of London brokers, the collapse of the silver market was due to the US not purchasing. The spokesperson for the US Treasury Secretary stated that the US authorities have repeatedly stated that they faithfully fulfill the provisions of the Silver Purchase Act, but it should not be forgotten that the Secretary of the Treasury previously stated that the US Treasury Department's monetary policy is based on a 24-hour basis. There has been no clear statement from official circles, so no one can say how long the US Treasury Department will remain outside the world silver market. State Department personnel are unwilling to criticize the claim that the US government's silver purchases are related to the Sino-Japanese situation. Congressional silver party members claim that they have not received news about the overall situation, but feel that the Treasury Department's actions do not indicate a permanent change in the US silver policy, and that the current situation is only temporary in nature. Someone suggested that the Secretary of the Treasury should specifically convene journalists to explain the silver situation. Undersecretary of the Treasury Ganston replied that there was no need to convene journalists specifically to discuss the silver situation. The Treasury Department is still fulfilling the provisions of the Silver Purchase Act and does not want to discuss the development of the world silver market or the strategies that the US needs to adopt to cope with this situation on a daily basis. (10th Reuters Dispatch)

(Washington) Treasury officials are still unwilling to criticize the silver issue today. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau did not go to the department this morning, but people in the Treasury Department claimed that the Secretary of the Treasury had very good information about the world silver market. The Secretary of the Treasury then arrived at the department, but did not want to discuss silver policy with journalists. However, a Treasury Department spokesperson stated that we are still implementing the Silver Purchase Act, but do not want to discuss the content of the plan or its current status. Washington is speculating about the relationship between the US silver purchase plan and the current world market. The US withdrew its silver purchase orders from London yesterday, and the London market completely stalled as a result today. There are widespread rumors here that the Treasury Department's position is as follows: (1) The Treasury Department is negotiating directly with China to purchase China's silver reserves. (2) The Secretary of the Treasury decided to exert great pressure on London in order to punish speculators. (3) The Treasury Department heard that a large amount of silver was being smuggled from China to Japan, and therefore stopped purchasing silver on the world market. Officials learned that the silver flowing from China to Japan in November was three times higher than in November 1934. It is said that the Treasury Department had previously promised to provide China with methods to improve the silver purchase, so as to minimize the damage suffered by China. (4) China sells silver in order to increase foreign deposits in US dollars and British pounds in order to stabilize currency prices, but the amount of sales exceeds the US's ability to absorb it. (5) The European war machine is gradually disappearing, and the United States cannot continue to buy silver without causing an unexpected surge in the British pound. For this reason, the Treasury Department suddenly terminated silver purchases. Financial observers with good information here believe that this statement is the most reliable. (10th National Telegram)

Impact on China's Monetary System

(New York) Today, some quarters here believe that the US Treasury Department's move to stop buying silver is the result of China's currency reform, believing that the plight encountered by the London silver market is due to China's large-scale sale of silver in London in order to obtain foreign exchange and stabilize its currency prices. The current difficulty for the US government is whether the US should raise silver prices to benefit the governments of Nanjing and Hong Kong. Senator Thomas made a statement in Washington today on this matter. Thomas was one of the leading figures in the silver purchase bill. He told guests today that the current silver market situation is the result of Britain wanting to control the world and linking China's currency to the British pound, which is detrimental to the United States. Britain sent Sir Ross to China, and Ross advised Nanjing that it would be best for China to adopt a managed currency system linked to the British pound, sell silver, and purchase gold. Thomas also said that they have been sucking us for a long time, and now uncovering their inside story is beneficial to the silver market and the United States. Therefore, the United States' suspension of silver purchases is indeed the right approach. Why should we help Britain solve China's problems, which will benefit Britain and harm the United States? From the standpoint of future stability of the world's currencies, the collapse of the silver market is an excellent thing. No one was buying in the New York silver market, and the price of foreign silver could not be set early today, but the final price was 63.75 cents, down one cent. The stock market opened erratically today due to panic caused by the silver situation. Later, the prices of various stocks were weak, especially metal stocks and railway stocks. The number of shares traded today was 2,341,000. (10th Reuters Dispatch)

Observations of London Newspapers

(London) The Financial News commented on the chaotic state of the silver market, saying, "The chaos in the silver market, what is the reason? It is impossible to speculate now, because the US government has not revealed its intentions at all. However, whether the silver policy has been ineffective in practice at the current stage, it is difficult to believe that the US government intends to abandon it entirely. The US government believed that raising silver prices could restore the purchasing power of the people of the Far East, but its expectations were completely inaccurate. This was proven long before China announced its new currency policy and abolished silver coins." The newspaper's conclusion raised the question, "Is the US move today a step to achieve the same purpose as in the past? Or is the entire concept of the silver policy wrong, and has President Roosevelt, who advocated this policy, begun to realize that the original view was misguided?" (11th Havas Dispatch)

Hong Kong Not Affected

(Hong Kong) According to reliable estimates, the Hong Kong Treasury currently has 85 million yuan in silver reserves, because the issuing banks have handed over all their ready cash to the Treasury. All the cash is in silver coins, and the number of large silver bars is very small. This morning, the world silver situation did not have much impact on the Hong Kong market, except that speculators bought US$550,000. (11th Reuters Dispatch)

(Paris) According to information obtained by our correspondent, British Undersecretary of State for Foreign Affairs Vansittart visited Prime Minister Laval late at night after the British Cabinet meeting yesterday and held talks. The discussions focused less on the content of the joint Anglo-French proposal and more on the impact of the proposal on the sanctions policy. In other words, if the Anglo-French proposal is accepted by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini but rejected by the Emperor of Abyssinia, should the oil embargo be implemented against Italy? It is generally believed that the British Cabinet believes that the solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute must be accepted by the League of Nations and approved by both parties. Therefore, if Abyssinia rejects the Anglo-French proposal, the oil embargo should still be implemented. Prime Minister Laval, on the other hand, is eager to avoid Italy's reaction to the implementation of the oil embargo. Therefore, he advocates that if the Emperor of Abyssinia rejects the Anglo-French proposal, he should bear part of the responsibility for the failure of the peace talks. Therefore, sanctions measures should not be tightened. (10th Havas Dispatch)

Any Suggestion to Reward Aggression Unacceptable to the Abyssinian Government; Preferring Resistance to Ceding Territory for Peace; British-French Plan Submitted to Both Parties; League of Nations Sanctions Committee to Meet Today

(London) According to reliable sources, the Abyssinian government has notified the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating, "The Abyssinian government deems unacceptable any solution to the dispute that rewards the aggressor." The notification further stated that the reason Abyssinia waited until the last minute to issue a mobilization order and prepare for war was due to the request of the British government. Abyssinia is now "willing to fight to the end and will never accept such a solution." (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Addis Ababa The Emperor, upon learning of the proposed solution to the Italo-Abyssinian dispute by British and French diplomatic authorities, immediately stated that Abyssinia would oppose any attempt to cede even a single foot of territory to the aggressor. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(Rome) Mussolini is expected to issue a response tonight regarding the British-French reconciliation plan, expressing considerable approval. The British-French plan has been submitted to Prime Minister Mussolini by French Ambassador Chambrun and British Ambassador Drummond successively. Thus, the gloom that has hung over Rome for months has suddenly seen the dawn today. (National Telegram, 11th)

(Paris) Today, it has been confirmed here that after Britain and France discussed and revised the peace plan agreed upon in Paris by the British Foreign Secretary and French Prime Minister Laval through diplomatic channels, the British government has expressed satisfaction with the peace terms. British Under-Secretary for Foreign Affairs Vansittart, accompanied by British Ambassador to Paris Clerk, visited the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs today to discuss the plan. When leaving the ministry, when approached by reporters, Vansittart replied, "We have reached a compromise."

The revised peace terms were telegraphed to Rome and Addis Ababa (the Abyssinian capital) last night. It is widely believed that the British government has requested the French government to explicitly announce that this proposal must be accepted by Italy, and also by Abyssinia and the League of Nations. Subsequently, a compromise satisfactory to the British government was reached. According to French sources, the revision agreed upon by both parties involves a significant reduction in the amount of land in Tigray Province ceded to Italy. The rights enjoyed by Italy within the land designated for Italian immigrants have also been revised, and the land remains under the sovereignty of the Abyssinian King. It is said that the British government considered the original terms to be too favorable to Italy. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

(London) According to what our reporter has learned, the points the Cabinet insists should be modified in the Hoare-Laval joint proposal are not of great importance. According to the new plan proposed by the Cabinet: (1) The area of Tigray Province ceded to Italy is smaller than in the original plan. In addition to Aksum, the "holy city," the district of Adigrat will also continue to be held by Abyssinia. (2) The zone in southern Abyssinia proposed to be permitted for Italian colonization should be managed by an Italian company. This company should be organized under a special license from the Abyssinian Emperor and supervised by a representative of the League of Nations. Furthermore, according to what our reporter has learned, the Cabinet insists that the modification of Abyssinian territory (i.e., the cession of Tigray Province to Italy and Abyssinia's acquisition of an outlet to the sea on the Red Sea coast) must be in the nature of a territorial exchange, so that Britain can avoid the suspicion of rewarding an aggressor. Figures in the Foreign Office believe that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will accept the plan proposed by Britain and France, but the Abyssinian government will certainly reject it, as can be clearly seen from the Abyssinian government's note to the Foreign Office tonight. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Reconciliation Amendment; Britain and France Reach Complete Agreement; Formally Submitted to Both Parties

(Paris) French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval announced today that the British-French plan to mediate the Italo-Abyssinian dispute has been submitted to the governments of Italy and Abyssinia today. (National Telegram, 11th)

(London) After the closest consultation between London and Paris by telephone, the British Cabinet approved the British-French plan to reconcile the Italo-Abyssinian dispute tonight. It is said that the main sticking point was a procedural issue. Britain insisted on submitting the plan to the League of Nations first and then notifying Italy and Abyssinia, but Laval rejected this. (National Telegram, 11th)

Eden and Laval Travel to Geneva Together; Sanctions Committee to Meet Today

(Geneva) The League of Nations Sanctions Committee will meet as scheduled tomorrow. It is said that France is advocating for a postponement, but Britain disagrees. It is expected that the British-French peace proposal will be discussed at tomorrow's meeting, but a concrete resolution on this matter is still far off. The plan will likely be transferred to the Sanctions Adjustment Committee or discussed at the League of Nations Council meeting next Tuesday. Eden is scheduled to depart for Geneva tomorrow via Paris. Regarding the proposed oil embargo against Italy, Russia, Romania, the Netherlands, Siam, Finland, Iraq, India, Ceylon, Argentina have not yet responded. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

(Paris) Although Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Hoare have agreed on a solution to the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, the question of what procedures the League of Nations will adopt remains unresolved. Laval will travel to Geneva tonight in the same car as British Minister Without Portfolio Eden. The two will discuss this issue on the train. At the same time, the Chairman of the League of Nations Council's Five-Nation Committee, Spanish representative Madariaga, is also on the train. Therefore, Laval and Eden will also be in contact with Madariaga. It is generally expected that the Eighteen-Nation Committee will delay discussion of the kerosene embargo on the grounds that Britain and France are conducting mediation, and will conduct negotiations with the relevant countries under the auspices of the League of Nations, based on the plan agreed upon by Britain and France in Paris. As for the Council's Five-Nation Committee, it was originally an organization responsible for mediation, composed of representatives from Spain (Madariaga), Britain, France, Poland, and Turkey. Previously, the recommendations put forward by the committee on September 18 were not accepted by Italy, causing it to stall until now. Now, it should continue its work to complete its success. In addition, the countries participating in the sanctions are all suffering because of the implementation of sanctions. When the above-mentioned negotiations begin, they will naturally feel that the shackles are lessened and can take a breath. However, the restoration of normal relations between those countries and Italy will only be possible after the proposals of Britain and France are accepted by Italy and Abyssinia. In short, the proposals agreed upon by Britain and France this time are sufficient to show that the two countries have made their best efforts to mediate the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Their concessions to Italy have reached their maximum limit, and their political possibilities cannot be increased further. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Sacrificing the Weak to Create Peace; Nothing Less Than a Death Knell for the League of Nations; Criticism from the Soviet Press

(Moscow) A Soviet observer believes that Britain is preparing to recognize the peace proposals of French Prime Minister Laval because Japan has repeatedly invaded China, so it does not want to be constrained by other matters in the Mediterranean, Africa, and Europe. Pravda said that if the League of Nations succumbs to British pressure and sacrifices Abyssinia to achieve this peace, then the British-French peace plan will become the death knell for the League of Nations. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

Eden Answers Questions in the House of Commons; Clarifies British Policy; Peace Proposals Based on Three Principles

(London) Minister Without Portfolio Eden answered questions in the House of Commons today regarding the Labour Party's criticism of the peace plan to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, stating that the British government still adheres to the principle that any peace proposal must be accepted by Italy, Abyssinia, and the League of Nations before it can be implemented. Labour Party spokesman Smith declared that if the rumored peace plan is even half true, it violates the principles of the League of Nations and abandons the position the government relied on in the recent general election. Eden responded, reiterating the British government's policy and emphasizing that the Paris proposal is only the first step in a long and complex undertaking. This proposal is based on three major principles: (1) the exchange of land, beneficial to both Italy and Abyssinia; (2) League of Nations assistance to Abyssinia to promote social, economic, and administrative development; (3) special facilities for Italian expatriates and Italian companies involved in Abyssinia's economic development. As for the peace terms reported in the newspapers, most are extremely inaccurate, and the rest are contradictory. The current content of the proposal cannot be made public because it is unprecedented to publish the content before it has been sent to the League of Nations or the countries concerned. We have never said that any party must accept this proposal, nor do we want to impose conditions on others. Our responsibility is to consult with the countries concerned to see if we can obtain a basis for peaceful negotiations to proceed. If this proposal violates the principles of the League of Nations, then the League of Nations should judge it to be incompatible, and we will obey the League of Nations without complaint. Eden continued, "I will go to Geneva tomorrow because the British government's policy is still based on its membership in the League of Nations. I will consult with representatives from many countries to jointly determine the best way to maintain the authority of the League of Nations." (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

(London) Regarding the government's response to King George V's address, after days of debate, the House of Commons finally passed the resolution by a majority of 281 votes to 139. Beforehand, Labour Party members had questioned the government, and Prime Minister Baldwin answered and concluded the debate, saying, "Regarding the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, we have never intended to act alone, nor do we intend to do so today. Although Minister Without Portfolio Eden will report to the League of Nations Council on the solution to the Italo-Abyssinian dispute agreed upon by the British and French diplomatic authorities, if the League of Nations Council does not adopt it, then Eden will be powerless to implement it, because Eden will find it difficult to force Italy and Abyssinia to accept this plan, and we do not know what decisions the countries concerned will make. However, if our efforts to mediate this time still yield nothing, then we must try again in the future. As for the consequences that the implementation of sanctions may cause, we must reconsider the entire problem. When we talked about the kerosene embargo, we originally thought it was simple and easy, but who knew that the complexity of the matter was extraordinary, because if we want to do something, we must ensure that the embargo can have a practical effect. Otherwise, empty talk will not help. In short, we will soon tell the gentlemen of the House of Commons all the experience we have gained from this mediation of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. At that time, the House of Commons and the national people will also consider what can be done in the future to advance the work of the League of Nations Council. That is all I can say to you tonight. In short, the policy we are currently following is completely consistent with the one we have always pursued. We are still responding to the League of Nations Council and following its lead, but we will never cross the line, because we only have two paths to follow: to fully assist the League of Nations Council or not to assist it at all. We must know how to choose between the two." (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Japan Insists on Equal Demands; Naval Conference Heavily Reefed; Japanese Representative Explains Reasons; Atmosphere at Meeting Not Good; Britain and America Form United Front; Harmony Unprecedented

(London) When the Naval Conference resumed this afternoon, Japanese Chief Delegate Admiral Nagano again explained the reasons for Japan's demand for naval equality, and the atmosphere at the meeting became particularly unpleasant. It is generally feared that a setback is imminent. The various delegations are now considering ways to salvage the failure. Reuters has learned that the opinions of the British and American representatives on naval limitations are in greater harmony than at any time in the past twelve months. All parties are now conducting tentative discussions, intending to grant Japan equality in principle within the scope of the Gentlemen's Agreement to preserve its prestige, but it will contain the nature of a tiered clause to prevent Japan from invoking it when it is actually building ships close to the level of Britain and America. This method will not be proposed at the meeting until discussions on a common higher limit prove to be a failure. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

(London) When the Naval Conference resumed this morning, it was reported that the spokesman for the British delegation, Jellicoe, extended the principles of the Washington and London Naval Treaties and made amendments appropriate to the changing international situation and the needs of each country. The British spokesman also suggested abolishing submarines. US Chief Delegate Davis reiterated the proposal to reduce the navy by 20% and said that the United States is prepared to explore any reasonable proposal. The conference will not reconvene until tomorrow afternoon, so that British Naval Minister Monsell can attend the cabinet meeting today. There will be noteworthy developments at tomorrow's meeting, as it is heard that the Japanese representative intends to explain in detail Japan's demand for naval equality. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

So-Called Common Maximum Limit; Britain and America Ask Japan to Fully Explain

(London) At the meeting of the First Committee of the Naval Conference yesterday, the representatives of Britain and the United States asked the Japanese representative to provide a more detailed explanation of the claims made by the country. According to what our reporter has learned, the Japanese representative will provide an answer when the First Committee continues its meeting this afternoon. There are several questions that the British and American representatives have raised to Japan: (1) Does Japan's so-called "common maximum limit" mean that the navies of weaker countries should be expanded to the level of the major naval powers, or should the forces of the major naval powers be reduced to the level of the weaker countries? In other words, does the method advocated by Japan aim to increase or decrease the forces of each country? Because so far, the Japanese representative has not provided any figures. (2) If Japan insists on requiring the navies of weaker countries to be expanded to the level of British and American forces, then Britain and the United States are eager to know whether Japan is prepared to announce its future shipbuilding program and whether this shipbuilding program intends to reach the level of the British and American navies. (3) Japan has not fully explained the reason why it believes that the balance system stipulated in the Washington Naval Treaty, which was considered appropriate in 1921, has been considered inappropriate since 1930. In addition, there are two points that Britain and the United States also want to understand, namely (a) whether the so-called "common maximum limit" applies equally to all naval powers; and (b) whether it applies to all types of warships. Since the representatives of Britain and the United States raised the above questions, some parties believe that no matter what method Japan's demand for naval equality takes, Britain and the United States will firmly oppose it at tomorrow's meeting, because this demand of Japan is not acceptable to Britain and the United States. The reason for asking it to explain it is to prove its unacceptable nature, so that it can be rejected in whole or in part. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Japan's Stance is Reasonable and Consistent

(London) The Japanese delegation to the Disarmament Conference held a meeting yesterday to discuss the explanation policy of Japan's claims at the first committee of the Disarmament Conference on the 11th. The results decided are as follows: (1) Regarding the right to equality of armaments, Japan's request to set a common maximum limit is a matter of course from the perspective of national dignity, but it is not only proposed because of adhering to dignity, but is based on the need to establish a national defense strategy and put forward a concrete request. Therefore, the proposal to nominally recognize the right to equality but actually reduce the amount of possession is absolutely opposed. This point is made with the extreme force of argument, given that there are claims abroad that demanding the right to equality is only a matter of face (1) The reason for demanding the right to equality, as stated at the exhibition, is to establish the principle of ideal disarmament, not threatening and not aggressive. Those who truly do not want to cause war in the world should be able to understand this reason. Naval power is free to move and does not threaten or invade, and it must be based on equal rights. (1) If the nations recognize Japan's claim, they are prepared to propose a numerical proposal for the common maximum limit of military strength, and its level must be kept low, and it is decided that this conference must make it a landmark conference in the history of disarmament. (1) The positions of Britain, America, Japan, France and Italy are different. The Japanese representatives are most concerned about the large reduction of high-level armaments. (1) During the transition period before the common maximum limit is realized, if it is long-term, the result will be to allow the ratio to be maintained during the period, so Japan cannot agree to the abolition or large reduction of offensive weapons, and it must be carried out in the short term. As for the discussion of numbers, it belongs to the public judgment of the meeting. For example, if its period is ten or fifteen years, it is actually too long. (Denstu Telegram, 11th)

Naval Treaty Expires Next Year; Japanese Navy Prepares for Major Maneuvers

Belgian Airplane Accident; Wing Icing Caused It; Eleven Passengers Died

(London) An airplane carrying passengers, flying from Brussels (the capital of Belgium) to London, crashed near the signal station of the Tatsfield-Bickley Airfield in Kent, England. A total of eleven people died, including seven passengers. The famous British designer of the Carden aero engine, Sir Carden, was also among them. It is now believed that the cause of the crash was icing of the wing. People near the crash site saw the plane flying low, its nose suddenly pointing downwards, and the fuselage turning over. The pilot apparently tried to ascend, but one wing touched the treetops of the Rutsy Hill. The entire plane was then destroyed, and the broken parts were scattered hundreds of yards around. The plane belonged to the Belgian Sabena Airlines, and it is said that the Belgian government is its main shareholder. The pilot and three other crew members were all Belgian. In addition to two British passengers, the remaining dead were two German men and women, and one Belgian. Other people nearby said they heard a huge shock at the time. They ran from their homes to the crash site and saw that the plane had been destroyed. They then moved out the bodies of several victims, one of whom was a woman whose limbs were incomplete. The bodies of the remaining people had fragments of the fuselage inserted into them. In addition to designing the Carden aero engine, Sir Carden was also known for designing army tanks. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

The Dream of Philippine Independence Rapidly Diminishes: An Article Published by Famous American Reporter Howard

(Washington) According to the opinion of Howard, director of the Howard newspaper chain and the American United Press, after the expiration of the autonomous government of the Philippine Islands in 1946, from the perspective of the Filipinos themselves, they will not be completely independent. Zhen, who is currently in Manila, published an article today stating that the dream of Philippine independence has rapidly diminished.

The issue of independence has been the biggest point of contention in Philippine political circles for 35 years. However, less than a month after the establishment of the autonomous government, it has reached a dead end. The Philippine Republic stipulated by the Independence Act and demanded by political leaders seems impossible to realize anywhere.

The expansion of the Japanese army, with the ambition to engulf the entire Far East, now casts a shadow over the entire Philippines. Therefore, the biggest political goal of the Filipinos has shifted from independence to seeking the safety of the freedom they have already obtained. The value of this safety has increased sharply, so the first step is to seek it under the American flag. The Filipinos do not want Japan's "Asian Monroe Doctrine," because this Japanese phrase is equivalent to "Asia for the Japanese."

Howard believes that if the situation does not change, in a few years, the US Congress will "be asked to make the autonomous government a permanent system, and determine its political and economic status as a territory. At the same time, the Filipinos have also begun to prepare to promote the commercial potential of the Philippines to the American political and business circles. Once the political status is determined and free trade between the Philippines and the United States is guaranteed, the economic mutual benefits will be unlimited.

The current anti-Philippine attitude of American workers can be eased by strict immigration laws. If Congress is afraid that Filipinos will cause trouble after joining, it can be stipulated in advance that they cannot be changed to a state system. If this propaganda still fails to arouse the interest of Americans, then the business leaders of the Philippines bluntly stated that they will ask the autonomous government to contact the United Kingdom and be willing to be a British colony. Britain would naturally welcome this proposal, because the Philippines is not only economically developed, but also can strengthen Britain's position in the Far East. If it unfortunately falls into the hands of the enemy, it will endanger Britain's entire position in China.

The above situation described by Howard is the opinion he collected from visiting the entire island and talking with leaders from all walks of life for a month. As for the general public, Howard said that they still cannot understand the situation in all aspects. They only know that after independence, they will be able to eliminate the chronic problems, and now they have practically achieved the goal of independence.

Therefore, they have deep faith in the current leaders. However, people who lead public opinion and are highly educated, except for some political figures, mostly admit that if the Philippines cannot be economically independent and lacks adequate national defense, there is no political independence to speak of. Even most political figures also admit that with the strength of the Philippines alone, it cannot achieve economic and national defense independence. However, they are limited by their positions and cannot publicly express it.

The Filipinos believe that their change of policy is not contrary to the policies of other countries related to the Pacific. Since Japan defied the League of Nations and invaded the Asian continent, the Far East policies of various countries have changed. When Washington and Manila considered the issue of independence in the past, they always believed that political independence and territorial integrity could be guaranteed by treaties. Now, judging from the situation in China, it has proved that this kind of guarantee is of no value in the Far East. Therefore, in addition to the surprise of the United States and the Philippines, the Filipinos also believe that changing the policy is not a breach of faith. Moreover, the Filipinos believe that the abandonment of independence is caused by forces that the Filipinos cannot control, because the Philippines is not willing to withdraw from the United States unless it is given a definite guarantee. At present, the American side has little understanding of all the resources and business opportunities in the Philippines, and is also unwilling to have more disputes overseas. Therefore, the Filipinos only hope that the United States will not force the Filipinos to accept independence only in name after giving independence to the Filipinos, and hope that the current nationalism in the United States is only a temporary conservatism caused by the recession. In the future, once the economy recovers and American business redevelops overseas, it will still retain the American market, and the Philippines will not be regarded as an exception. (National Telegram, 10th)

Quezon's Written Response

(Manila) President Quezon today gave a written reply to Howard's report, declaring that he has sworn to abide by the Philippine Constitution, which stipulates the independence of the Philippines in 1946. In any case, our responsibility to create a nation is to strive to make us self-reliant and self-sufficient in all aspects in a very short period of time. (National Telegram, 11th)

Attention of the US Army Authorities

(Washington) Army Department authorities today stated regarding Howard's views on Philippine independence that any action to make the Philippines a part of the United States must first be passed by Congress. The Army Department pays close attention to Howard's views, but cannot directly criticize them because it has not received official notification. However, it is said that Howard's statement is a clear report of the original views on the Philippine issue. (National Telegram, 11th)

Congressmen Express Their Opinions

Congressmen generally believe that the permanent US affiliation movement of the Filipinos will cause economic problems, and the outcome is difficult to predict. Roughly speaking, the sugar, vegetable oil, and milk industries will continue to demand complete separation, while the textile, automobile, and machinery manufacturing industries will support affiliation. Observers said that geographically, agriculture is distributed throughout the country, and congressmen representing rural areas have always been able to win. Senator Tydings declared that he doubted that Congress and the American people would agree to maintain the status quo in the Philippines. The United States has allowed independence for 35 years, and the Filipinos' demand for complete independence has not stopped. Last winter, he went to the Philippines specifically to inform the Filipinos of the difficulties after independence. He warned them about this matter. Then the Philippine Congress passed the Constitution, which was finally approved by the United States, and then held elections, and the autonomous government was established. Regarding the facts stated in Howard's report, Tydings said that he did not believe that Japan intended to take the Philippines, and the Filipinos decided on their needs. A spokesman for the American Federation of Labor said that he believed that most Filipinos hoped for complete independence. A spokesman for the American Farm Bureau also said that the Filipinos had already accepted independence, and the Farm Bureau would not participate in the movement to change that policy. Senator Franci said that he felt that the Filipinos' request for independence should be recognized. Congressmen who participated in the founding ceremony of the Philippine autonomous government should be able to determine the future attitude of Congress towards the Philippines. Senator McClay said that if the United States cannot manage the Philippines' foreign affairs, army, navy, air force, customs, immigration, and issue of national debt, he does not approve of a permanent autonomous system. He opposed granting independence after visiting the Philippines and reported this to the Senate. He firmly believes that an independent government will not defend its country, but if the United States abandons all property and control of the island, he feels that it is better to withdraw completely. If we should not control the important parts of the Philippine government after the transition period, it is better to let the Filipinos take care of themselves. (National Telegram, 10th)

International Commercial Telegram

Reuters Special Commercial Intelligence Telegram, December 11

Exchange Rates

Sterling-Dollar: The London foreign exchange market this morning still felt the repercussions of the silver market turmoil. The price of sterling continued to weaken against the dollar and the French franc, as there was concern about a lack of dollars if the United States decided to stop buying silver. However, around noon there was a firm atmosphere. The opening price of sterling-dollar was 4.92125, lower than the US-UK closing price yesterday by 0.001875. In the first hour, it fell by 0.000125. At noon, it continued to fall by 0.00025 to 4.9204375. In the next hour, the trend turned firm, rising by 0.000125 at one point to 4.9205625, after which there was no change.

Sterling-Franc: The opening price fell by two pounds to 74.69 francs. In the first hour, it fell by six pounds. At noon, it continued to fall by six pounds to 74.57 francs. In the next hour, there was no change. At two o'clock, it rebounded by three pounds to 74.60 francs.

Gold and Silver

Sterling Gold: The London gold price rose by two and a half pence today to 141 shillings and two and a half pence due to the weakness of the pound.

Sterling Silver: The London silver market today was indeed less turbulent than yesterday, and the number of sales decreased significantly. Most sellers limited prices. The spot price is expected to be revealed today, but the forward price may be difficult to settle for a while.

US Silver: The Mountri silver market opened lower by more than 200 pounds, because the London market still has no US purchases, and the Bombay silver market has weakened again.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: Although the Liverpool cotton market was stable, the New York cotton market opened down several pounds. People's hearts were disturbed by the white silver storm. Although the cotton market base was stronger than before, there were not many transactions. Johnston, manager of the Public Reserve Agency, stated that the agency's policy has not changed. Fertilizer sales have been very large recently.

Sterling Cotton: The price in the Liverpool cotton market did not change much, as merchants are awaiting the results of the US Supreme Court's actions. At 1:00 PM, the price for the January term was 6.37, up three pounds.

Sterling Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market opened stable this morning, expressing sympathy with foreign markets. However, trading was lighter after the transaction, and the price fluctuation was small, because merchants are waiting for the outcome of the white silver situation. There are no new features in the market. At 1:00 PM, the price for the December term was 5 shillings and 11 pence 625, lower than the closing price yesterday by 0.0025. Corn was also firm, with the price rising by three pence.

US Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened slightly lower, and then fell slightly again due to the low Liverpool telegrams, the instability of the silver market, and the improvement of the European political situation. The miscellaneous grain market was stable, with prices close to yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market situation was stable this morning. The April-June term opened unchanged, with the price at 6 shillings 4375. At noon, it rose by 0.0625 to 6 and a half pence.

New York: New York rubber opened up several pounds due to better London telegrams. After the price increase, the price stabilized due to purchases by colleagues.

Securities

New York: The New York stock market opened mixed and lower, with metal stocks being particularly loose. After a period of instability, the market progressed vigorously, and most stocks rose above yesterday's closing price. Automobile, department store and public utility stocks were stable. Oil stocks fell slightly. The average price of the Dow Jones 30 industrial stocks opened at 142.24, up seven pounds. The prices are as follows:

(Nanjing) Pudley returned to Beijing on the morning of the 11th after surveying the Huaibei waterway, and reported to the Economic Commission. According to him, the opening of the Wuhe waterway has no technical difficulties. A plan has been drafted and submitted to the commission. Work can begin as soon as the commission and the Salt Affairs Bureau agree. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

(Nanjing) Stampar, a health advisor to the League of Nations, left for Peiping on the morning of the 11th and then to Shanxi to inspect the province's health undertakings. He will stay for about ten days before returning to Beijing. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Jiangsu Province Strictly Prohibits the Purchase and Transportation of Silver

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Government recently received confidential reports that silver coins and silver objects in various counties are being bought and transported by unscrupulous people. This is due to the negligence of prevention in various counties. On the 11th, it reiterated the ban, strictly investigated and dealt with it, in order to maintain the national monetary system. If private purchase and transportation are found, in addition to confiscation, they will be punished according to law. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Train on Beining Road Delayed in Peiping

(Peiping) The fourth special express train between Peiping and Yushuguan on the Beining Road collided with a car at Yangcun Station at 4:40 PM today. The car wanted to cross the railway and travel south. The car suffered slight damage, and the train stopped at the time. It was delayed by one hour when it arrived in Peiping. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Wu Yiting and Others Engage in Activities in Tianjin

(Tianjin) Wu Yiting of Xianghe, Wang Jianzhong of Baodi, and Jie Zu of Qingcheng, Hebei Province, have drawn up ten articles of association for the preparatory office of the People's Congress and issued a declaration. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Japanese Warship Anchored in Tianjin Sails to Tanggu

(Tianjin) The Japanese destroyer "Kiku," anchored on the riverbank of the Japanese concession here, has decided to set sail on the morning of the 12th and anchor in Tanggu due to the shallow water and the imminent freezing of the Haihe River. The Tianjin office of the Lushun Fortress has begun to work, and it is said that it is specifically responsible for contacting ships sailing to the Tianjin-Tanggu area (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

More Than 100 People Freeze to Death in Tianjin Due to Extreme Cold

(Tianjin) The weather here is extremely cold, especially at night. More than 107 people have been certified by the court as having frozen to death within a few days. In the Nanshi area, another twelve beggars were found frozen to death on the morning of the 11th. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Sichuan Province徵徵徵conscripts Labor for Road Construction

(Chengdu) To reorganize the completed roads in Sichuan Province, the Road Supervision Office of the Xingying Headquarters sent engineers to various counties to explain the main points of voluntary conscription. Currently, 41,000 civilian workers have been conscripted from the eleven counties along the Chengyu section of the Sichuan-Guizhou Road, and work has started one after another. It is expected to be completed in January next spring. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Remnant Bandits in Eastern Fujian Rely on Dangerous Terrain to Resist Stubbornly

(Fuzhou) Remnant bandits in the Tai Lao Mountain and Wu Yang Mountain area in eastern Fujian are stubbornly resisting on dangerous terrain. Yang Baogu, commander of the 50th regiment of Zhang Qiong's brigade, personally led his troops to the front yesterday to take on the attack. Chen Peiyu's troops were specifically responsible for blocking and suppressing them, and it was decided to completely clear the bandits in one fell swoop. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

(Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Zhangzhou Prefecture Rice Donation Incident

(Xiamen) The Provincial Government replied to the Chamber of Commerce and various trade associations on the 10th, stating that the rice donation in Zhangzhou Prefecture is only 100,000 yuan per year. The elimination of heavy taxes and miscellaneous levies, compared to 300,000 yuan or more in Tongzhou Prefecture alone, means that the elimination is greater than the reduction. It is hoped that they will support and assist. Rice transportation in Zhangzhou has been suspended for ten days. The tax bureau is persuading them to resume transportation, with registration required for a month. If the tax is not withdrawn, it will be paid retroactively. Rice merchants in Zhangzhou and Xiamen are exchanging opinions. In another ten days, more than 3,000 packages of rice were transported from Tongfu and Shanghai to Xiamen, preventing food shortages. On the 10th and 11th, prices fell from 8.5 yuan to 8.2 yuan. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Sakamoto Goes from Hong Kong to Shantou

(Xiamen) Sakamoto Ryuki, the foreign affairs director of the Taiwan Governor's Office, went to Shantou from Hong Kong on the 10th and will arrive in Xiamen on the 12th. He will stay for a few days before returning to Taiwan. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Denies that Diplomatic Sections Will Be Established in Provincial Governments

(Hong Kong) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed Gan Jiehou, denying the decision of the Sino-Japanese Association to establish diplomatic sections in provincial governments. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Zhejiang Province Restricts Passengers from Carrying Silver and Copper Coins

(Hangzhou) The Zhejiang Provincial Government stipulates that any passenger leaving or entering the province may not carry more than fifty silver coins or more than one thousand copper coins. If the number exceeds this amount, they should be ordered to exchange it locally for legal tender, otherwise it will be confiscated. This measure was approved by the Ministry of Finance on the 11th and has been telegraphed to all counties and cities for compliance. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Luo Zhuoying's Troops Build Roads

(Hangzhou) 12,000 soldiers of Luo Zhuoying's 18th Army are building the Lishui-Songyang Highway. It is scheduled to be completed within 20 days and open to traffic by the end of the year. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

The National Government on the 11th issued an order approving the resignation of Liu Heding, commander of the concurrently held 56th Division, from his concurrent position. This order also appointed Liu Shangzhi as the commander of the 56th Division. This order also approved the resignation of Yang Sang, a member of the Mongolian Local Autonomy Political Affairs Committee, from his post. Political Committee for Hebei and Chahar Provinces: Definite Establishment Process

Powerful Japanese Figures in Beiping and Tianjin Have Agreed; Committee Member Candidates Await Central Government Decision and Announcement

Beiping Correspondence: The measures for dealing with the situation in North China have been discussed repeatedly by Chen Yi, Xiong Shihui, Xiao Zhenying, Qin Dechun, and others for days. Internal opinions only reached a consensus on the evening of the 5th. Xiao went to Tianjin on the morning of the 6th to negotiate with powerful Japanese figures in Tianjin. It was not until the 7th that the agreement of powerful Japanese figures in Beiping and Tianjin was obtained. Thus, the measures for stabilizing the situation in North China could be determined. On the 8th, the situation took a sharp turn for the better. It is reported that the organization of a "Political Committee for Hebei and Chahar Provinces" has been finalized in Beiping, with one chairman and several members. He Yingqin and Song Zheyuan have reported the situation to the Central Government.

The proposed location for the Political Committee for Hebei and Chahar Provinces is the former Ministry of Foreign Affairs during the Beiyang government era, which was previously the site of the Reorganization and Political Council. After the Central Government issues a clear order for its establishment, organizational regulations will be drafted. The area under the committee's jurisdiction will include Hebei and Chahar Provinces, as well as Beiping and Tianjin Municipalities. The nature of this committee is important in two aspects: (1) In name, it must absolutely not break away from the Central Government to maintain national sovereignty; (2) It must adapt to the local environment to stabilize the current situation. Currently, both the Chinese and Japanese sides have agreed to these principles. In the future, in addition to establishing various departments or sections, the committee will also hire individuals familiar with East Asian affairs to serve as consultants.

The establishment date of the Political Committee for Hebei and Chahar Provinces has not yet been determined. The initial decision was to have 19 members, but on the 9th, it was changed to 15. After discussions that night, it was increased again to 17. The list of members has also been telegraphed to the Central Government and will be announced after being approved by the first Central Political Conference on the 11th. There are some discrepancies between the names of the committee members announced by the Chinese and Japanese sides. The Chinese side announced the following: Chairman Song Zheyuan, members Wan Fulin, Shang Zhen, Wang Yitang, Liu Zhe, Jia Deyao, Li Linyu, Hu Yukun, Gao Lingjue, Xiao Zhenying, Qin Dechun, Zhang Zizhong, Cheng Ke, Zhou Zuomin, and Men Zhizhong, totaling 15 people. The Japanese side's announcement did not include Jia Deyao and Li Linyu but included Li Tingyu. According to Li Linyu, he has not had any contact with any party on this matter; it may be a mistake for Li Tingyu. Li Linyu is the president of Sino-French University, while Li Tingyu is a former subordinate of Wu Peifu who once served as the governor of Henan Province. The Japanese announcement also included Qi Xieyuan and Xu Songming. Xu is the president of Beiping University. According to sources close to Xu, Xu has refused to serve as a member, and if his name appears, he will submit his resignation. Shang Zhen told reporters that he had not been informed of his appointment as a member of the Political Committee for Hebei and Chahar Provinces and will not take the position. The affairs of the Hebei Provincial Government have been concluded and can be handed over at any time. The 32nd Army under his command will be returned to the Central Government. In the future, he personally wishes to travel abroad to broaden his knowledge.

The Political Committee for Hebei and Chahar Provinces will internally establish three departments: Secretariat, Finance, and Political Affairs. Each department will have sections, and each section will have groups. If necessary, a secretary-general may be established in the future. After the committee members are announced, they will be assigned to the two departments to work. The staff of each department will be transferred from those who previously served in the Military Sub-Committee and the current Beiping-Tianjin Garrison Headquarters.

Qin Dechun and Xiao Zhenying went to Jurentang at 9:00 AM on the 10th to meet with He Yingqin to discuss everything. After meeting with He, Qin and Xiao took a car to the Summer Palace to meet with Song Zheyuan.

Xiong Shihui, Chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, came north with He Yingqin earlier to deal with the situation in North China. Now that things are generally settled, he felt the need to report to the Central Government urgently, so he left Beiping by train at 3:05 PM on the 10th to return to Nanjing. (10th)

Student Parade in Hangzhou

—Expressing Sympathy for Students in Beiping—

A visitor from Hangzhou reported that in response to the demonstration by students in Beiping against the autonomy of North China, Zhejiang University students convened a joint meeting of over 400 students at 9:00 PM last night (the 10th) and resolved to: (1) Send a telegram in support of the demonstration by university students in Beiping; (2) Send a telegram to all schools across the country to respond in unison; (3) Contact students from various schools in Hangzhou to form a propaganda group to promote opposition to North China's autonomy to the public. The propaganda team of Zhejiang University students went to designated locations at 7:00 AM this morning (the 11th) to carry out propaganda. Later, upon reading reports that the demonstration by students in Beiping on the 9th resulted in a bloody tragedy, representatives from secondary and higher schools in Hangzhou were urgently convened at 10:00 AM for a meeting. It was decided to hold a large parade at the Hubin Sports Field at 2:00 PM this afternoon to oppose all autonomous organizations in North China that falsely claim to represent the will of the people. The representatives returning to Hangzhou notified the students of their respective schools to participate. The meeting began at 3:00 PM, with over 10,000 students from Zhejiang University, Advanced Institute of Technology, Advanced Institute of Agriculture, Art Academy, Chinese Medicine Academy, Zhijiang University, Hangzhou High School, Hangzhou Junior High School, Municipal High School, Girls' High School, Hongdao School, Huixing School, Girls' Vocational School, Zhongshan School, Finance School, Feng's Girls' High School, and other schools in attendance. Representatives from each school formed a presidium to determine the meeting's proceedings and elected Shi Eryi as the temporary chairman. He reported the purpose of the meeting and the situation in North China, stating that the students of Hangzhou were united in support of the government. The students then shouted slogans and began their parade, departing from the Hubin Sports Field, passing through Yingzi Road, Sanyuanfang, Jianqiao, Minquan Road, Xinmin Road, Dongjie Road, Yanjiao, Zhong'an Bridge, Yanling Road, Hubin Road, and then gathering again at the Hubin Sports Field to disband. They shouted slogans along the way, and the order was very good. Military and police authorities dispatched teams to maintain traffic. At 8:00 PM, an ad hoc meeting of representatives from various schools was convened to discuss sending telegrams to support and comfort the dead and injured classmates in Beiping and to organize a joint student organization in Hangzhou.

Provincial Inspectors Come to Songjiang One After Another

In order to inspect the administrative status and progress efficiency of various counties, the Provincial Government specially dispatched inspectors Shen Yong, Ning Bojin, and Ke Bojin. After completing their inspection in Nantong, they transferred to Songjiang on the 10th and met with County Magistrate Li at the County Government. They then stayed at the Xin Songjiang Society. Inspector Ning focused on the baojia system and accompanied the first district office for inspection on the morning of the 11th, and set out to randomly check the baojia. The county's inspection of the police force was originally scheduled to be held in Kunshan District. However, the provincial department considered winter defense to be important and it was not convenient to transfer troops, so the inspection was stopped. Therefore, Inspector Ke was dispatched to undertake the mission of inspecting the police security team of the Public Security Bureau. Inspector Ke, accompanied by County Magistrate Huang Zhifang, inspected the headquarters of the 12th Security Brigade and its subordinate teams, as well as the internal affairs of the Public Security Bureau on the afternoon of the 11th. At 2:00 PM, he gathered the soldiers of the security team and the police of the Public Security Bureau at the public sports field to be inspected by Inspector Ke. Ke gave a public speech with many words of encouragement. Inspector Ning, accompanied by Huang Zhifang, Section Chief of the County Government, hired a car to go to Sijing to inspect the baojia. It is reported that they still need to go to Fengjing and other places for inspection on the 12th before returning to the province to report.

Changshu: Fake Son of an Official Escorted to Yixing for Investigation

On the 3rd of this month, a young man named Yu Feihe came here. Because he claimed to be the son of Yu Jingtang, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, the Public Security Bureau heard about it and welcomed him to the city, opened a high-end hotel for him, held a banquet to wash away the dust, and sent people to guide him to tour the mountains and rivers. After three or four days, there were no flaws. Unexpectedly, when examining Yu's photo, the matter was revealed. The young man then admitted that his surname was Chu. His family was notified, and his mother, Wang, came to Changshu to take him back. The bureau insisted on having him post bail, which was delayed for three days. Until the 10th, his mother found a store to provide a guarantor and was completing all the procedures. Unexpectedly, the Department of Civil Affairs called and instructed not to release him because the young man dared to impersonate the son of the Director. The newspapers everywhere have already published this, and Director Yu is very angry and instructed to escort him back to his original home in Yixing for investigation. Therefore, the bail could not be completed here, and his mother burst into tears. On the 11th, the five bureaus escorted him to the Yixing County Government.

Suzhou: Zhang Yipeng Goes to the Province to Request Collection of Rent

The Wuxian Relief Institute, the Public Funds and Public Property Management Office, and the Warehousing Committee, because this year's rent collection has not improved, which has a great relationship with the overall finance and public funds, specially elected Zhang Yipeng as a representative to bring a petition to the province on the 10th to ask the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance to strictly pursue the rent. It is reported that the total public and private land rent in Wuxian is about four million, and the current income is less than one million, which is very different from last year.

Wuxi: German Driver Runs Over and Kills a Village Child

At about 11:00 AM on the 11th, two Germans, a man and a woman, were driving a black-plated car with license number 1480 from Shanghai along the Xihu Road to Wuxi. When they were traveling between the 19th and 20th bridges near Yangjianchang, A Rong, the ten-year-old son of Wang Longshi, a villager from Chao Dongxiang, was returning home from Yangjian Town. Because he failed to avoid the car in time, one of his legs was broken, and his head and chest were seriously injured. He died on the spot, which was unbearable to witness. Later, the family of the deceased came forward to negotiate. As a result, the Germans paid 60 silver dollars to settle the matter. The car that caused the accident immediately returned to Shanghai.

Ningbo: Theft, Arson, and Suicide Out of Fear of Punishment

Yang Bingcao, a warehouse clerk at the Bank of Communications on Jiangbei Wai Ma Road in this port, had been working as a cook at the home of Yu Runquan, the manager of the bank. In April of last year, with Yu's promotion, he transferred to the bank to work as a warehouse clerk. His wife, Song, had a daughter and lived on the upper floor of the Qiashun Restaurant at No. 67 Erheng Street. At about 2:00 AM on the 9th, Yang suddenly had a thieving heart. Taking advantage of the deep night and silence, he dug a hole in the wall of the manager's office in the bank and entered the vault, stealing 19,000 yuan in banknotes and silver dollars. He sneaked home and hid them in a small jar outside the room, covering it with firewood. After the incident, he poured kerosene on the mailbox and set it on fire, intending to destroy the evidence. After setting the fire, he rushed to the home of Xiang Shiyuan, a clerk at the bank, to report. At that time, Wu Qinhai, the chief of the fourth precinct, was on patrol and passed by the bank, catching sight of the flames inside the window. He immediately knocked on the door to warn them. The employees of the bank were awakened and rushed to put out the fire, which was quickly extinguished. Then, they found that a large sum of money had been stolen from the vault. They smelled the pungent odor of kerosene and knew that someone had done something wrong. They reported it to the captain of the detective team, who came to the bank to investigate and questioned the workers one by one. When they questioned Yang Bingcao, Yang panicked and falsely claimed that he had returned to the bank from a mahjong game on the Ningxing ship and discovered the fire. The detectives took him to the ship for questioning, and the matter was exposed. Seeing that the situation was bad, Yang jumped into the river and committed suicide while getting off the ship. The 19,000 yuan in banknotes and silver dollars he had stolen were found by the police in his home, without any loss. Yang's body had not been found as of the morning of the 10th.

Ministry of Finance: Crackdown on Private Hoarding and Sale of Silver Coins

Yesterday, an instruction was issued to the money shops to establish measures for the crackdown; the Money Shop Guild has already notified all shops to comply.

The Industrial Society reports that the Ministry of Finance, considering the recent frequent occurrences of unscrupulous merchants privately collecting silver coins in the hope of selling and smuggling them abroad for profit, which has a significant impact on the monetary policy, issued a special instruction yesterday to the Shanghai Money Shop Guild to convene its members and instruct the cigarette and exchange businesses to convene their members to discuss and establish measures for cracking down on private hoarding and sale of silver coins. They are expected to comply conscientiously. Details are as follows:

Ministry of Finance Instruction

Ministry of Finance Instruction Qian Zi No. 2085 states: Since the implementation of the legal tender (fabi), the use of cash is prohibited, as has been widely announced by this Ministry. Recently, there have been instances of unscrupulous merchants raising prices to buy silver coins, hoping to sell and smuggle them abroad for profit. These merchants only seek private gain, disregarding the overall situation, and willingly break the law, which is extremely regrettable. This Ministry has also issued a general order to all political, military, police, and customs agencies to strictly investigate and punish them according to the law. It is understood that the members of the Guild and the cigarette and exchange businesses inevitably exchange silver coins in their business of exchanging silver coins and copper coins. However, they should follow the legal tender exchange procedures and promptly submit them to the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications for exchange into legal tender for use, and should not hoard them privately. However, since there are many members in these businesses, it is inevitable that some may be tempted by private gain and hoard the collected silver coins privately, hoping to sell them, which constitutes illegal behavior. The Guild should immediately convene its members and instruct the cigarette and exchange businesses to convene their members to discuss and establish measures for cracking down on private hoarding and sale of silver coins to ensure compliance and protect the monetary policy. The agreed-upon measures should be submitted to the Ministry for review. This order is hereby issued.

Money Shop Notification

After receiving the order, the Shanghai Money Shop Guild issued a special notification yesterday to all shops that have not joined the association to comply. The notification states: "Respectfully, we received Ministry of Finance Instruction Qian Zi No. 2085, which states (original text omitted). Having received this order, we find that all member shops of this Guild are involved in remittance and exchange and do not engage in the business of subsidiary currency and exchange. All hard currency sealed after November 4 has been submitted to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications. We will submit a separate reply to the Ministry of Finance and comply with the order to inform the cigarette and exchange businesses' guild to prepare measures. We hereby record and transmit the order. We respectfully request your shop to jointly agree with all non-member shops to properly establish measures for cracking down on private hoarding and sale of silver coins and reply to the Guild for transmission. This matter concerns a Ministry order, so we hope you will promptly discuss it properly."

The Yinwei Loan Reduced to One Million Yuan; The Contract Will Be Revised After Negotiation

The New Voice Society reports that the Yinwei loan signed by the Shaanxi Provincial Government on November 14th of last year amounted to a total of 1.5 million yuan, consisting of 450,000 yuan from the Central Bank, 350,000 yuan from the Bank of China, 250,000 yuan from the Bank of Communications, 225,000 yuan from the Shanghai Bank, and 225,000 yuan from the Jincheng Bank. It was stipulated that the funds would be disbursed as needed for the project, with 200,000 yuan in the first phase from April to June of the 24th year, 600,000 yuan in the second phase from July to September, 400,000 yuan in the third phase from October to December, 250,000 yuan in the fourth phase from January to March of the 25th year, and 50,000 yuan in the fifth phase from April to June. Since the signing of the contract, the Yinwei project has not commenced according to the original dredging date, so no funds have been used.

Renegotiation and Reduction to One Million

Lei Baohua, Director of the Shaanxi Construction Department, now that the Yinwei Project Office has been established and the dredging project is about to begin, consulted with the Xi'an branches of the five banks that provided the loan, believing that the Yinwei project did not require 1.5 million yuan. It was decided to reduce the amount to one million yuan, using the entire revenue from the Jinghui Canal, Luohui Canal, Yinwei water levy, and the provincial business tax as collateral. The funds are to be used solely for the various expenses stipulated in the Yinwei Irrigation Project Plan and are not to be used for other purposes. The monthly interest rate remains at eight percent. The lenders will nominate two representatives to serve as members of the Shaanxi Water Conservancy Expenditure Management Committee, and a special auditor will be appointed to audit all income and expenditure related to the loan.

Contract Revised with a Term of Five Years

The Xi'an branches of the lending banks telegraphed their head offices in Shanghai for approval. The revised loan contract was formally signed on the 9th, with terms similar to the previous one. It was stated that the Yinwei loan contract signed on November 14th of the 23rd year of the Republic of China was void. The five lending banks nominated the Bank of China as the chief representative, disbursing funds as needed for the Yinwei project, without specifying a deadline or amount. The loan term remains five years. After the completion of the Yinwei project, it will be named the Weihui Canal.
