Treasurer's Report: Summary of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Financial Situation

Land tax and license revenues have declined significantly; this year's projected surplus is approximately 300,000 yuan; the Police and Public Works departments lead in cost-cutting; the future may be even more difficult than the past.

The Finance Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council recently held a meeting to discuss the accounts of the various departments of the Council for the first nine months of the year, ending in September. At that time, the Treasurer of the Municipal Council made an oral presentation on the financial situation of the Council. The minutes of the Committee meeting were reviewed at yesterday's regular meeting of the Council. The details of the Committee's discussions are excerpted below.

In his report to the Finance Committee, the Treasurer stated that although the accounts of the various departments of the Council had been submitted, some points related to the summary of the results must be pointed out. Under the ordinary budget, there was a surplus of 1,823,533 yuan up to the end of September, and the projected surplus for the whole year was 35,810 yuan. However, this figure would not accurately reflect the actual financial situation until the end of the fiscal year. For example, on the revenue side, the full amount of the land tax for the year has already been included, while on the other hand, the utility fees for various public utilities under public and municipal services have not yet been included because they are settled semi-annually. In addition, the total municipal rate and the extra-Settlement roads special rate under ordinary revenue were approximately 563,000 yuan less than projected for the first nine months of the year. The reasons for this are approximately (1) fewer new buildings than in previous years, (2) lower rents, and (3) more vacant properties. The revenues from the wharfage dues and license fees have also decreased. However, it is gratifying that the shortfall has been more than offset by the cost-cutting measures in the expenditures of various departments.

The Treasurer then, at the request of the Chairman, gave a more detailed oral presentation on his submitted report. He stated that the purpose of the compilation of the financial report for the first nine months of the year was to inform the various departments and their affiliated committees of the expenditures that have already been confirmed for the first nine months of the year so that they could be more prudent in their expenditures in the remaining months of the fiscal year, and to allow a preview of the results of the year's operations. Regarding municipal revenue, the city has suffered greatly from the impact of the widespread economic downturn. The sources of revenue, such as land tax, license fees, and other revenues, are far below expectations, as mentioned above. However, the increase in vacant properties and the decrease in new buildings seem to be showing signs of improvement compared to the past. According to his estimate, the total revenue from various sources for the year will be approximately 1.25 million yuan less than budgeted last year.

As for ordinary expenditures, according to the Treasurer, the expenses of various departments in 1934 were reduced by approximately 1.1 million yuan compared to the budget due to austerity measures. However, the austerity measures taken by various departments this year have been even more stringent than last year. Therefore, according to the statistics compiled by various departments, the amount saved is approximately 1.6 million yuan, excluding the expenses of the Telephone Special Committee, which are approximately 93,000 yuan. The largest source of these savings is the Police and Public Works departments. Of course, the savings from other departments are also considerable. In the Police Department, the number of foreign personnel and prison personnel is 44 less than the quota. Other parts of the department have also taken similar austerity measures. There are also many similar situations in other departments. As for the Public Works Department, the total amount of savings is second only to the Police Department. However, the department implemented austerity measures earlier than other departments. Major construction projects, such as road construction and improvement, and other activities, can be temporarily suspended. However, if other departments want to reduce expenses effectively, they must start by laying off employees. The Treasurer also stated that the heads of the Public Works and Police departments, and the heads of other departments, have cooperated fully in these cost-cutting measures.

The Treasurer said that the most important aspect of the expected outcome of this year's ordinary budget is to find ways to achieve a surplus. According to his estimate, after setting aside appropriate reserves, the surplus for the year will be approximately 300,000 yuan. Last year, the projected surplus was 360,000 yuan, while the actual surplus was approximately 700,000 yuan. Considering the unprecedented difficulties faced this year, if this result can be achieved, it can be considered satisfactory.

Furthermore, regarding the budget for 1936, if there is a surplus this year, it will have a substantial impact on the budget carried over to the following year. In the opinion of the Treasurer, the difficulties ahead will be far greater than those experienced in previous years. If the municipal taxes continue to be levied at the current rate of 14%, the initial deficit will reach a huge 3.5 million yuan. This year's ordinary budget has already been reduced significantly compared to last year, and next year's budget will inevitably be even tighter than this year's. However, this is related to public works. If austerity measures continue indefinitely, the final result will be a decline in efficiency and a deprivation of social well-being. Furthermore, the projected surplus for this year refers to the balance after the allocation from the reserve fund, while the initial deficit of 3.5 million yuan for 1936 mentioned above refers to the balance before the allocation from the reserve fund. The amount of the deficit will naturally be reduced after the reserve fund is used. During the Finance Committee's discussions, one of the members mentioned the foreign staff of the Municipal Council's remittance allowances. The Treasurer also made some remarks regarding the calculation and handling of the allowances.

Regarding the extraordinary revenue and expenditure accounts, the Treasurer stated that at the beginning of the year, the construction expenses proposed by the various departments had been reduced to the lowest possible level. Even at the ratepayers' meeting, the Chairman had indicated that the construction expenses in this year's budget were much lower than last year's. The projects that were already underway and had to be completed, and the road construction that had to be carried out, accounted for almost the entire budget. However, although the budget had been reduced to the lowest possible level, thanks to the strong cooperation of the Director of the Public Works Department, the actual expenditure of the department was still able to be reduced significantly, by approximately 1.5 million yuan. The suspension of various construction projects was expected. However, given the financial difficulties this year, the benefits of this move should not be overlooked.

As for the sources of funds for the various construction expenses, the issuance of municipal bonds was impossible. Therefore, it was necessary to slightly increase the overdraft on the temporary sterling accounts and sell some assets at favorable prices to meet the expenses. Furthermore, the mortgage terms for the 1933 Shanghai Telephone Company loan were very favorable. The company had already repaid 1 million yuan in installments at the end of June of this year, and an equivalent amount would be repaid by the end of the year.

Regarding the Municipal Council's debts, the Treasurer mentioned the 6% municipal bonds of 1925 and 1926. The Treasurer stated that at the beginning of the year, he had been instructed by the Board of Directors to agree with the bondholders' trustees that the repayment of the 1925 bonds would be postponed because the maturity date was still 20 years away. Given the current situation, it would be useless to repay these two types of bonds according to the initial repayment schedule stipulated in the trust deed, i.e., by December 31 of this year and the following year. Furthermore, the trust deed had previously been amended to give the Council the right to manage the fund for the repayment of the bonds and to allow a grace period of five years in order to avoid the need to immediately deposit cash to await an uncertain need. However, this arrangement does not harm the interests of the bondholders because the bonds can be redeemed at any time after the first optional repayment date with six months' notice. The timing of the redemption will depend on the financial and bond market conditions and whether it is in the Council's interest. It is not appropriate to sell its assets on a fixed date to repay the debt. The future course of action will depend on the future financial situation. According to the arrangement that he had agreed upon with the trustees, the debt repayment fund should be extended for another five years so that the total amount of the debt repayment fund can reach 5 million yuan. However, as mentioned above, the interests of the bondholders will not be affected, and there will be no conflict with the Council's right to choose the date of redemption. Therefore, the arrangement that he had agreed upon with the trustees should be approved by the Committee.

The members of the committee expressed their agreement with this move.

The Chairman then discussed the issue of various allowances for Municipal Council personnel and said that the Treasurer should be asked to report on the current austerity measures and future policies at the end of the year. The Treasurer said that the matter had been thoroughly investigated and that he would report on the outcome at a later date. However, in his opinion, this matter is very complex and requires consideration of both economy and fairness, and is closely related to the satisfaction and efficiency of current contract employees.

The Huiping Vessel Has Been Missing Since Leaving Haizhou; An Investigation Is Underway

The Shanghai Huaitong Company's Huiping vessel left Haizhou for Yantai five days ago and has not been heard from since. It is possible that the vessel encountered a storm and took refuge, resulting in its disappearance. Details are as follows:

Five Days Without News Since Leaving Haizhou

The Huaitong Shipping Company, located at 44 Guangdong Road, has a large shipping business in North China, with Yantai as its base. Its Huikang, Huichang, and other vessels operate in the Beiyang region, while the Huiping vessel also operates between Zhifu and Haizhou. The Huiping vessel left Haizhou fully loaded with cargo this time, bound directly for Yantai. Normally, it should arrive in 36 to 48 hours, but it has been several days without any news. The company is very worried and has telegraphed Haizhou to inquire and telegraphed the Shanghai office to inquire about the vessel's whereabouts.

Whether to Avoid the Wind, Various Parties Inquire

After receiving this news yesterday evening, the reporter inquired with various parties and learned that the Huiping vessel had indeed left Haizhou fully loaded with miscellaneous goods and has been missing for five days. It is still difficult to say whether it has gone missing. After consulting with Director Tang Danhua of the China Ship Insurance Association, it was stated that the Huiping vessel had indeed left Haizhou and has not been heard from since. There has been fog and strong winds on the sea in recent days. It is possible that the vessel is taking refuge elsewhere. The vessel does not have wireless equipment, so communication is more difficult. The China Ship Insurance Association has an insurance policy for it of 30,000 yuan. In addition to reporting to the Insurance Association, Huaitong Shipping has sent telegrams to various places to inquire about the vessel's whereabouts.

Ningjing Escapes Danger and Passes Wusong

The Vessel Ran Aground Due to Heavy Fog Near Jiangzikou, But Fortunately Escaped Danger and Passed Wusong as the Tide Rose

The Ningjing vessel of Ning Shao Company, with a load of 1,693 tons, originally operated in the Yangtze River ports. Recently, it was leased to Haizhou to load salt and transport it to the Yangtze River ports for unloading. The vessel arrived at the Jiangzikou sea area at 5:00 AM on the 10th of this month. Due to the fog, navigation was difficult. At that time, the vessel ran aground on a shoal near Jiangzikou. Because it was heavily loaded with salt and had a deep draft, the captain's attempt to free the vessel was unsuccessful. He telegraphed Shanghai for assistance. The company was planning rescue measures when they received another telegram from the vessel yesterday afternoon, saying that fortunately, the tide had risen greatly in recent days. During the high tide on the night of the 10th, the captain took the opportunity to put the engine in reverse and free the vessel from the shoal. There was no need to send a rescue vessel. It was expected that the Ningjing vessel would pass Wusong at 3:00 PM on the 11th and enter the Yangtze River.

Two Announcements from the Jianghai Customs

One Regarding the Procedures for Importing Narcotic Drugs, and One Regarding the Revised Implementation of Diesel Import Tariffs

Announcement 1: The Jianghai Customs issued Joint Announcement No. 1480 yesterday regarding the procedures for reporting the import of narcotic drugs, stating that an order had been received from the Ministry of Finance issuing the revised regulations for the management of narcotic drugs. The revised points are listed below: (1) Import permits for narcotic drugs transported from Germany and Switzerland will no longer be issued by the Customs. (2) The reporting of narcotic drugs, toxic substances, strychnine, etc., will only be permitted through Shanghai. (3) The Central Health Testing Institute will be solely responsible for all narcotic drugs, toxic substances, strychnine, etc., transported from abroad or sold domestically. Import of such drugs requires submission of a license from the Ministry of Interior. Domestic sale requires a purchase permit from the Central Health Testing Institute. All merchants are hereby notified. Director Tang Haian, Customs Commissioner Ba Runsen.

Announcement 2: The Jianghai Customs issued Joint Announcement No. 1481 yesterday regarding the periodic revision of item 529A of the import tariff, stating that an order had been received from the Ministry of Finance stating that item 529A of the import tariff will be revised and implemented from January 1, 1936, as follows: Import tariff item 529, diesel oil: (A) Specific gravity at 20 degrees Celsius above 0.90, flash point (according to the Creese test) above 95 degrees Celsius, and kerosene content below 60%. You are hereby instructed to comply accordingly. All merchants are hereby notified. Director Tang Haian, Customs Commissioner Ba Runsen. (New News Agency)

Opening of Zhabei Soup Kitchen: Request for Municipal Government Funding Assistance

Poor people are suffering from hunger and cold, urgently needing relief. The Social Affairs Bureau forwards the request to the Municipal Government for review and approval.

The Zhabei Charity Organization, due to the increasing number of poor people, is complying with orders to prepare for winter relief by opening a soup kitchen. We respectfully request that the Municipal Government approve and allocate funding. This is a special report to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. The report states that on the 22nd of last month, the Bureau issued instruction No. 2920, which briefly stated that due to the severe floods in various provinces this year, businesses and industries are exhausted, and the poor are struggling to find food and clothing. The situation this year is unique, and the organization is required to prepare for providing soup and other relief efforts early. In response to this order, the Zhabei Charity Organization recognizes that Zhabei is a gathering place for coolies and poor people. Every winter, we open a soup kitchen, and the elderly, weak, and children flock to it for food, often numbering in the hundreds. In this cold winter, a bowl of hot porridge is enough to extend their lives. Moreover, due to the economic downturn, many people have lost their jobs. Many factories, large and small, in Zhabei have frequently stopped operations, and even silk factories are mostly shut down due to a lack of raw materials. The sight of the general poor and suffering people, hungry and cold, is heartbreaking. We have no choice but to open the soup kitchen early to save these starving and freezing people. We plan to quickly repair the stoves, cauldrons, and houses at the No. 2 Soup Kitchen on Liuying Road, fearing that the freezing weather will hinder us. It is noted that the Zhabei Charity Organization has been allocated over two thousand yuan from the municipal government's revenue every winter to fund the soup kitchen. Last year, the mayor ordered the Finance Bureau to allocate one thousand yuan for relief. It is certain that the number of poor people eating porridge at the soup kitchen for half a year will be numerous, no less than in previous years. Furthermore, due to the state of the economy, it is difficult to raise donations. We earnestly request that the mayor, who loves the people like his own children, show compassion for the many suffering people and provide special relief. We believe that the Director of the Bureau is deeply concerned and spares no effort in relieving the poor. Therefore, we specifically submit this report, earnestly requesting that you review it and quickly forward it to the mayor, who will promptly order the Finance Bureau to allocate two thousand yuan annually for relief, so that we can open the soup kitchen early and save the hungry and cold, suffering people. We await your urgent instructions. Respectfully submitted to Wu, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has already submitted the report to the Municipal Government based on the situation.

Dismembered Body of a Child Discovered on Qimei Road

At 7:50 AM yesterday, the dismembered body of a child, about two or three years old, was discovered inside a bamboo fence west of the Guangzhou Leather Factory behind the temple on Qimei Road, east of Zhabei. Only the upper half of the body was found, severed neatly below the chest, seemingly cut off with a knife. Therefore, it was impossible to determine the child's gender. The body was discovered by Liang Wanquan, a worker at the factory, who was quite surprised and immediately reported it to the Linping Road Police Station. Police were dispatched to investigate and confirmed the report. A crowd gathered to watch, with some speculating that it was the child of a migrant worker who died of illness, and out of superstitious fear of reincarnation, they resorted to this cruel act. Others speculated that it was a small hostage who was killed after negotiations broke down. Opinions varied and no conclusion was reached. In the afternoon, Xu Jinlin, the local bailiff, reported the case to the local court, requesting an autopsy.

English Consulate Police Court Continues Hearing: Case of Two Police Officers Throwing a Chinese Man into the River; Police Car Driver Testifies to Witnessing the Incident; Unwavering Testimony Despite Repeated Questioning by Lawyers

According to the Zi Lin News, Peters, a Western police officer from the Ji Jiaxing Road Police Station in the Public Concession, and Jute, a probationary police officer, are accused of throwing a beggar named Mao Debiao (transliteration) into the Hongkou River on December 1st, causing bodily harm. Mao died in Renji Hospital on Friday morning of last week. An autopsy the following day confirmed that he died of pneumonia, which was aggravated by being immersed in water. The case was first heard by the English Consulate Police Court last week, as both defendants are British citizens. The court reconvened yesterday morning (the 11th) to continue the hearing. Four witnesses were called to testify, including two Chinese police officers, one Chinese clerk from the police station, and one Russian police officer. First, Chinese police officer No. 1728 testified that he saw a sick beggar on Xinji Bang Road on the morning of December 1st and reported it to the Jiaxing Road Police Station. Thirty minutes later, he returned to the spot, but the sick beggar was gone. He also stated that the beggar he saw at Renji Hospital did not look the same as the one he had initially seen. Next, Chinese clerk Yuan testified that his duties at the police station included recording events and answering the phone. Around 2:45 AM on December 1st, he received a report from Chinese police officer No. 1728 about a beggar lying on the side of the road and recorded it in the register. Police officers Peters and Jute were in the room at the time, and Chinese police officer No. 3067 drove them out of the police station. Yuan further identified the text he had written, but stated that the additional note below, "Arrived, beggar had left," was not in his handwriting but was written by Peters. The hearing continued at 2:15 PM in the afternoon. The Russian police officer was called to testify. His testimony was very brief, stating only that Peters initially ordered him to go and detain the beggar at the police station but then said that he (Peters) would go himself. Next, the police car driver, Chinese police officer Du No. 3067, who drove Peters and Jute to Xinji Bang Road to collect the beggar that day, testified. The police officer was questioned by the lawyer for over two hours but remained steadfast in his testimony. He firmly stated that on that day, he drove the two police officers to their destination. The two got out of the car and went into the alley, then brought a beggar back. The beggar was placed horizontally on the running board, and Peters also stood on the running board. They then drove to the middle of Feilun Road at the intersection of Yalu Road and Youheng Road. The two police officers ordered him to stop. Peters then grabbed the beggar's right leg and right arm, while Jute grabbed the left leg and left arm. They walked to the riverbank and threw the person into the river. Prosecutor McNair immediately questioned Du to get the truth. Du replied that this was what he had seen with his own eyes. Defense lawyer Rickes also questioned Du, but Du remained steadfast in his testimony, stating that after the beggar fell into the river, he shouted wildly. Because he did not leave the car, he did not see whether he landed in the water, only heard his cries. Rickes continued to ask why he did not report the truth after returning to the police station. Du replied that the two were his superiors, so he could not do that. He only explained everything when he was questioned by the police inspector on December 2nd. After Du finished his testimony, the court adjourned and scheduled the next hearing for Saturday morning.

To ensure that no innocent person is wronged and no guilty person is let off. Sentencing scheduled for the 17th.

After several court hearings presided over by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, the defendant vehemently protested his innocence and presented evidence to the contrary. Presiding Judge Zhang, for the sake of caution and to ensure that no innocent person is wronged and no guilty person is let off, notified detectives from the French Concession Police Department to accompany the defendant to the victim's home for on-site inspection the day before yesterday. They also went to No. 9 Route Magy, where the robber was shot dead, to investigate and ordered him to demonstrate what happened. They returned to the court after two hours. At noon yesterday, Judge Zhang came to the Criminal Division to continue the hearing. The plaintiff and defendant still testified as before. After the court appointed a lawyer to defend the defendant, it announced the conclusion of the hearing and scheduled sentencing for the morning of the 17th. The defendant remains in custody awaiting instructions.

Legal action for Inheritance Claims against Concubine of Li Jingfang

Yesterday, evidence was taken from a witness, and Li Jiaxing and others must still be summoned for questioning.

Li Jingfang (Zi Bohang), the former Qing Dynasty minister, died in Dalian last autumn. Before his death, he wrote a letter of instruction regarding the distribution of his family property to his children and grandchildren to avoid disputes over property in the future. After his death, his concubine, Ms. Wu, learned that the letter stipulated that she would receive 23,000 yuan for her old age. This spring, she requested the money from Bohang's eldest son, Guo Tao, grandsons, Jia Ji and Jia Xing, and Zhou Mengwen, the witness in the letter of instruction, but has not received a penny to date. Ms. Wu hired a lawyer, Zuo Detou, and filed a lawsuit for embezzlement against Li Guotao and the other three, which has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui held a court hearing. Except for Li Jiaxing, who has tuberculosis, the other defendants were all present. The witness, Li Guoxiao, though suffering from hemiplegia for a long time, followed the summons and arrived at the court in a hired car, with his driver crying. Because he could not stand on his own feet, Judge Liu allowed him to speak from inside the car during his testimony. First, the plaintiff, Li Wu, stated the facts of the lawsuit, saying that the old master (referring to Jingfang) stated in the letter of instruction that she would receive 23,000 yuan for her old age, but it had been embezzled by the defendants. Therefore, she was filing a lawsuit. She was 25 years old when she became a concubine, and followed them to Dalian in 1927. Last March, she returned to Shanghai first due to illness, and the old master passed away in September. The defendants did not tell her, so she only heard the news this January. The old master told her before his death that if something happened to him, she could ask Guotao for her old age money. But when she asked for the money she was due, Li and his sons first claimed they did not know, then said she had already taken it. In reality, she only learned about the letter of instruction from others. Defendant Li Guotao testified that his late father's letter of instruction was written in the presence of his children, grandchildren, and concubines. His father personally handed over the property to each person, and the plaintiff's money was also received at that time. Li Jiaji's testimony was similar to Guotao's. At this time, the plaintiff's attorney, upon learning that the defendant Zhou Mengwen would be questioned, requested that the defendants be separated to ensure impartiality. The court then ordered the two Lis to wait outside the court and questioned Zhou, warning him not to favor any side. Zhou agreed and testified that he is currently the manager of the Liji Shipping Company in Wuhu and has long had friendship with Li Bohang. Li's property in Wuhu has always been managed by him. On December 24, 1932, Li wrote the letter of instruction disposing of his family property in Dalian, and he was also present. Therefore, Li asked him to sign the letter as a witness after the distribution was completed. However, the transfer of property took place upstairs, and he did not witness it. Judge Liu then compared Li Guoxiao's letter to Zhou and Zhou's reply with Zhou's testimony and made some discoveries. He then repeatedly questioned Zhou. Next, witness Li Guoran was questioned, who testified that he suffers from hemiplegia, but his mind is still clear. However, others think he has a mental illness. His father's letter of instruction was written in Dalian. Because he was ill, he was not present, so he did not know whether the plaintiff had received her money. This spring, the plaintiff came to him and said that she had not received the money she was due, so he wrote to Zhou Mengwen to inquire about it. Because the plaintiff often bothered him, he intended to mediate and have the six brothers each give 500 yuan, collecting 3,000 yuan to settle the matter. The court then scheduled a follow-up hearing for the afternoon of the 18th of this month, summoning defendant Li Jiaxing and witness Li Guohua to appear for further questioning.

Major Fire on Hengfeng Road, Zhabei Last Night: Over Eighty Thatched Houses Reduced to Ashes; Three Men Burned in the Fire and Sent to the Hospital for Treatment; Whether There Were Fatalities Still Needs to Be Investigated Today

There were approximately two hundred thatched houses for the poor at the intersection of Hengfeng Road and Yu Tong Road, Zhabei. At approximately 9:50 PM last night, a fire suddenly broke out in the middle of the thatched houses. Because the thatched houses were close together, twenty or thirty houses were on fire within a blink of an eye. For a time, people shouted and order was in chaos. The general coolies rushed to salvage mats, bedding, and old clothes from the fire pits, fleeing in panic. The sidewalks along Hengfeng Road were all occupied by these people as places of rest. Fortunately, the Fenglu Police Station in charge was nearby, so upon receiving the news, they immediately notified the fire department to dispatch fire trucks to rush to the scene to put out the fire. However, because the weather was dry and the wind was strong, forty or fifty more houses were affected in less than half an hour. At that time, the flames soared and were unapproachable. Fortunately, the firefighters bravely put out the fire, preventing it from spreading further. The fire was completely extinguished at around 11:00 PM. As a result, approximately eighty thatched houses were burned down, and three men were found to have been burned in the fire. They were sent to Renji Hospital by ambulance for treatment. However, it is not yet possible to determine whether there were fatalities, as it was dark, and the embers had not been extinguished. It is necessary to wait until work begins this morning before it can be clarified. The cause of the fire is currently under investigation.

Municipal Council Appeals: Chen Bingwei Accused of Fraudulently Posing as a Doctor; The Circumstances Are the Same as Those of Lawyers Without Licenses; The Defendant Claims That There Was No Negligence in His Medical Practice

Chen Bingwei, a 36-year-old Cantonese man, has not obtained a doctor's license or studied at any medical school, but claimed to be a doctor of medicine, specializing in venereal diseases, skin diseases, hemorrhoids, and other ailments. He set up a clinic at 613 Sichuan Road and falsely used the name of James Duncan, a professor at a certain medical college, to deceive patients. Recently, he was discovered by Dong Zhaobin, a Chinese detective from the General Inspectorate of the Public Concession, and was prosecuted in the First Special District Court for the crime of fraudulently obtaining property. After the trial, he was declared not guilty. During the appeal period, he paid a bail of 2,000 yuan. The Legal Department of the Municipal Council, dissatisfied with the judgment, filed an appeal with the Second Branch of the High Court through lawyer Ru Baoyi. Yesterday afternoon, Trial Judge Zhao Zhengchong, together with Associate Judges Zhou and Jiang and Prosecutor Lin, opened a criminal court to hear the case. First, lawyer Ru, representing the police department, stated the reasons for the appeal, saying that due to the special circumstances in the concession, the Provisional Regulations for the Amendment of Doctors could not be applied, resulting in unlimited restrictions on the qualifications of doctors. This has led to a general lack of medical knowledge, claiming to be doctors and hanging out signs to practice medicine, harming patients. It is not superficial. The defendant Chen Bingwei has neither studied at a medical college, nor has he obtained a license, but he claims to be a doctor of medicine and an expert in several diseases, and he also falsely uses the name of Duncan to dazzle people. To know a doctor, his skills must surpass that of a medical officer, and the patient must know whether the doctor has academic talent or is a doctor. The police department cannot use administrative sanctions to crack down on these swindling doctors, so they have no choice but to use judicial procedures to crack down on them. Moreover, the defendant's behavior is sufficient to constitute the crime of fraud under criminal law, but the original trial ruled him not guilty, which is difficult to accept. Therefore, an appeal is filed with your court, requesting that the original judgment be revoked and an appropriate sentence be imposed. Chen Bingwei's defense was that his brother graduated from a medical school in Guangdong and practiced medicine. He worked as an assistant for about ten years, so his skills and knowledge are very rich. Although he did not have a hot photo, it was said to be fraudulent, it has been several years, there has been no negligence, so please reject the police department's appeal. The police lawyer then cited that any lawyer who has not obtained a license and hastily performs his duties is willing to commit the crime of fraudulently obtaining property, so the situation in this case is actually the same. Finally, after mutual debate by the two lawyers, Prosecutor Lin Wo Peng rose to express his opinion, believing that the appellant was highly suspected of committing a crime and requested that he be punished according to the law. Trial Judge Zhao then declared the debate concluded and scheduled the sentencing for the afternoon of the 18th.

Judge Convicted of Committing a Crime: Forging Official Documents; Sentenced to One and a Half Years

Feng Jiasheng, 35, from Minhou, a clerk of the former Fujian High Court Prosecutor's Office, was ordered to temporarily serve as a student prosecutor at the Minhou Local Court. Gangsters Broke into a Construction Factory at Night and Stole Hemp Bags, Exposed

They Tied Up the Watchman and Threatened Him with Knives, Indian Police Patrols on the Street Led to the Capture

The Qiye Construction Factory, located on Connaught Road in Shanghai West, had a watchman because the factory contained goods and there was no work at night. The watchman, a Ningbo native named Yang Qingfeng, was hired to guard the premises at night. Around 3 AM yesterday morning, a gang of four, Wu A'gen, Lin Qiaosheng, Chai Shankang, Feng Guo, and others, carrying weapons, went to the factory. They first snuck in through the bamboo fence gate and stole 191 hemp bags of cement, throwing them out over the fence one after another. Unexpectedly, because the night was late, everything was quiet, and these people took a long time to throw the hemp bags, they woke up the watchman Yang Qingfeng. Just as he was about to investigate, the gang realized they had been discovered. Fearing their plan would fail, they decided to strike first. They rushed in, pulled out knives, and threatened him. They used ropes to tie Yang's hands and feet to the bed, and stuffed a cloth into his mouth, preventing him from making noise. Wu and the others were then able to calmly hire rickshaws to transport the hemp bags elsewhere. They also locked the door of the watchman's shed from the outside. Unexpectedly, two Indian police patrols, numbers 410 and 41, passed by at that moment. Seeing Wu and the others transporting hemp bags in the middle of the night, their actions seemed suspicious, so they went forward to question them. The gang was nervous and fled in different directions. Only Wu A'gen and Lin Qiaosheng were arrested on the spot. The others, Chai and Feng, escaped. The police then entered the factory, released Yang, and together with the stolen goods, took everything to the Gordon Road Police Station. At 9:30 AM, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin prosecuted them according to Article 330 of the Criminal Code for robbery. Then, the watchman Yang Qingfeng filed a complaint about the previous events. When questioned, Wu and Lin confessed that the plan was conceived by Chai and Feng, who were still at large, and that they were only lookouts. Judge Wu Zehan reviewed the confession and ordered Wu and the others to be remanded in custody. The case was adjourned to next Monday for further hearing.

Zhang Siyun, Who Specializes in Selling Partridge Vegetables, Sued

The Plaintiff Accused Him of Breaching the Contract, the Verdict Was That the Defendant Was Not Guilty

The Hongxing Pharmacy is famous at the time for specializing in selling the children's medicine "Partridge Vegetables". Its head office is in Guangzhou. Recently, because business is booming, a Hongxing Pharmacy branch was established at 743 Nanjing Road in Shanghai, with Zhang Siyun as the manager. Now, Zhang was suddenly sued in the Criminal Court of the First Special District by the representative of Hongxing Foreign Firm, a Japanese man Takeuchi Heiten, and lawyers Huang Yuping and Huang Zengjie, for breach of trust and violation of Article 342 of the Criminal Code. They also filed a civil lawsuit, requesting the court to order him to repay the security deposit of 2,000 yuan and the contract penalty of 50,000 yuan. The reason for the lawsuit was that the defendant Zhang Siyun had signed a contract with the plaintiff on April 24 of this year, appointing the plaintiff as the general agent for Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and the three Northeastern provinces, to sell "Partridge Vegetable" medicine for a term of five years. At that time, the plaintiff paid a security deposit of 2,000 yuan. Article 3 of the contract stipulated that the defendant should deliver 100,000 packages of "Partridge Vegetables" by August 15 of this year. Article 6 stated that if the defendant established a branch in Shanghai, the plaintiff's consent must be obtained. Article 7 stated that if either party breached the contract, they should compensate the other party with a penalty of 50,000 yuan. Now, the defendant established a branch in Shanghai without the plaintiff's consent, which was a violation of the contract and a criminal offense, hence the lawsuit. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan presided over the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. The defendant was absent, and lawyer Jin Ximin appeared in court to defend him. The plaintiff's lawyer then rose and stated the above situation, saying that the plaintiff was currently away from Shanghai and could not attend the hearing, requesting a postponement. The defendant's lawyer, Jin Ximin, rose and said that even if the facts listed in the plaintiff's indictment were true, they were of a breach of contract and were entirely within the scope of civil matters. Moreover, the authenticity of the contract was questionable, and the seal on the contract seemed to be forged. Therefore, the defendant denied having ever signed the contract. However, the plaintiff knew this situation and had once filed a petition with the court on October 24 of this year, requesting mediation, which failed. Now, they suddenly changed their target and filed a criminal lawsuit, which was unreasonable and unjustified. They should request that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed. Judge Wu reviewed the case and ruled that Zhang Siyun was not guilty, and the plaintiff's civil lawsuit was dismissed.

The Pi Han Shelter Will Begin Receiving People, Charity Sends Letters Encouraging Support from All Sides

The Shanghai Charity Federation announced that the Pi Han Shelter will begin receiving people on the 26th. The letter stated: "The market is depressed this year, industry and commerce are sluggish, rural areas are bankrupt, and the number of unemployed civilians is increasing. In addition, after the floods in various provinces, disaster victims are flocking to Shanghai, without clothes or food, urgently needing relief. The Pi Han Shelter, which our association has organized for many years, should be held as usual. After several meetings, it was decided to start receiving people on the 26th of this month. If the weather is colder, it will be advanced accordingly. The Chaozhou Guild Hall at the South Railway Station will be used as the first shelter, and the Chao Huishan Villa on Xietu Road will be used as the second shelter. Once the two shelters are full, we will find more houses to expand. However, the Pi Han Shelter has no dedicated funds and relies entirely on donations. We have received donations and subsidies from you in the past, and your merits are immeasurable. This year, the number of people needing shelter will be greater than in previous years, and the need will be even greater. We sincerely ask you to donate generously to maintain the shelter. We would be grateful for your kindness. At this time of severe cold weather, poor people are suffering from hunger and cold. The Pi Han Shelter's expenses, in addition to the 2,000 yuan subsidy from the municipal government, are far from enough, as donations from various charities are still being collected. We hope that all sectors will donate generously. There is a great need for cotton clothing, blankets, and rice, which we hope can be sent to the Renji Hall so that the shelter can be established and start receiving people as soon as possible, which would be a great merit."

Miss Su Zengxiang, the second daughter of Mr. Su Renquan, a member of the Jiangsu Provincial Assembly and a progressive figure in education in Chongming County, graduated from the Tongde Medical School. She practiced medicine in Shanghai for many years with remarkable achievements. Robbed Silver Necklace and Strangled to Death, the Juvenile Was Interrogated, Convicted, and Sentenced Lightly to 15 Years in Prison

Gui Lin, the eight-year-old son of Zhou Qiu, a Taizhou woman who lived in a thatched shed in Zhoujiaqiao, west of Wusong Town, was playing in the nearby fields on the afternoon of November 14th. Ma Jinshan, a neighboring juvenile, noticed that Gui Lin was wearing a silver necklace. Ma, tempted by the sight of money, used a cloth strap to strangle Gui Lin to death. He then robbed the silver necklace and went to Laoshicheng Silver Shop on Songxing Road to exchange it for three yuan and six jiao. After Zhou Qiu, the deceased's mother, found out the above situation, she reported it to the police station in charge, who arrested Ma Jinshan and recovered the stolen goods. The Chuditou District Court Prosecutor's Office interrogated and detained him, and sent personnel to verify that Zhou Gui Lin had indeed been strangled to death. It has been reported in previous newspapers. Now, it is known that the case has been clearly investigated by Prosecutor Lei, and a public prosecution has been filed for murder. The day before yesterday afternoon, Judge Tan Zhuohong opened a court for trial and ordered Ma Jinshan to be brought to court. Ma Jinshan, who was 17 years old and from Taizhou, said that he was wronged. The official said, "You have confessed in the Public Security Bureau and the Prosecutor's Office. Today, you still want to deny it. You are young, but you are extremely cunning." After repeated questioning, Ma Jinshan confessed that he had been gambling and lost one yuan. He was being forced to pay it back, and he had no money to pay. When he saw Gui Lin wearing a silver necklace, he decided to steal it. He was afraid that Gui Lin would tell his mother, which would inevitably lead to negotiations, so he tightened the cloth strap around his throat. He said that he was too drunk that day and his nerves were confused, so he accidentally injured Gui Lin to death. He asked for leniency. The judge obtained the confession, considered the facts to be clear, and considered it to be the end. Yesterday, he ordered Ma Jinshan to be brought to court to announce the verdict. Considering that the defendant was still young, he was leniently sentenced to 15 years in prison as a warning. After the sentence was pronounced, he was taken into custody to await the execution of the sentence.

The Radical Nature of the Rent Reduction Tide in Northern Shanghai

After the false rumors occurred in Northern Shanghai last month, the residents moved away. Although some have moved back recently, they are only a small part of the sub-tenants, less than one-tenth of the usual number. In the neighborhoods north of Bazilu Road, only one-tenth or two-tenths of the sub-tenants remain. As for the sub-sub-tenants, there is not a single one left, and it is unlikely that anyone will rent there in half a year. The sub-tenants are overburdened, so on the 8th of this month, all the tenants of Yongfeng Lane, Heng'an Lane, Dade Lane, and Xinxiang Lane went to the Shanghai Northern Rent Reduction General Federation of the Zhongshan Fellow Association to hold a rent reduction meeting. The meeting was chaired by the two old gentlemen Peng. The meeting decided: (1) To send a letter to the owners of the four lanes to waive the rent for November and December according to the precedent of rent reduction; (2) To change the rent collection from January to 60% or 70%; (3) To send an official letter from the Federation to the owners of the four lanes for consent; (4) When necessary, gentlemen Zhuo and Peng will be sent to negotiate the rent reduction policy with the owners. All the official letters have been sent out yesterday.

Zhang Guinian's False Accusation Case Judgment, False Accusation and Forging Documents Result in Two Months in Prison, Manager and Clerk of Hua Sheng Factory Declared Not Guilty

Xin She Yun: Zhang Guinian, a clerk at the Ningbo Siming Bank, and his nephew Zhang Yanqing jointly opened the Yong Hua Sheng Sales Office last year. Zhang Guinian provided a 10,000-yuan bond to promote various electric fans from the Shanghai Hua Sheng Electric Factory. Later, the uncle accused the nephew of embezzlement and was involved in litigation in the Yin County Court. Later, due to a large debt owed to the Hua Sheng Factory, the factory filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai First Special District Court, and the defendant Zhang Guinian and Zhang Yanqing were jointly ordered to pay the plaintiff's debt of 6,645 yuan, 6 jiao and 7 fen, and interest at an annual rate of 5% from August 4, 1935, until the end of execution. The litigation costs were borne by the defendants. Zhang Guinian was not satisfied with the verdict and appealed, but was also rejected. He then intended to deny the debt and falsely accused the manager of Hua Sheng Factory, Ye Youcai, and the clerk Xu Qiaoqi, of forging documents. The court held a hearing on the 19th of last month. The defendants filed a counterclaim. The case was postponed due to the absence of the plaintiff. On the afternoon of the 10th, Xiao Xie Fen, a judge in the Criminal Court No. 2 of the Special District Court, heard the case. The counterclaimant and lawyer Cai Liu Cheng, and the plaintiff and lawyer Feng Mei Xue, arrived in court on time. After Judge Xiao carefully examined the case, the attorney Cai of the counterclaimant strongly refuted the plaintiff's misty accusation and stated the reasons for the counterclaim. He then declared in court that the counterclaimants Ye Youcai and Xu Qiaoqi were not guilty. Zhang Guinian was found guilty of false accusation and sentenced to two months in prison, suspended for two years.

Bureau of Social Affairs: Disaster Relief Funds to Continue Distribution Tomorrow; Policyholders Willing to Donate Remaining Funds to Aid Disaster Victims

According to the Huadong News Agency, after the January 28th Shanghai War, the Zhabei Disaster Area Insurance Association, on behalf of insured policyholders in the war-torn area, claimed fire insurance premiums from the Shanghai United Fire & Marine Insurance Co., Ltd. Except for the first batch of compensation of 20,000 yuan, which was allocated last winter under the auspices of the Bureau of Social Affairs and distributed to various disaster-stricken households, the second batch of 20,000 yuan will also be distributed to each household at the Zhabei Charity Organization on Datong Road on the 13th and 14th of this month. Each disaster-stricken household will receive a relief fund (i.e., fire insurance premium compensation) of six yuan. There are still over a thousand disaster-stricken policyholders. (Calculating based on the second batch of relief funds of 20,000 yuan, there is still a surplus of over 10,000 yuan.) They have received notification letters from the Bureau of Social Affairs, along with a receipt, instructing each policyholder to sign and stamp, fill in the address noted during communication, and come to the organization to collect the funds at the appointed time. Public announcement is hereby made.

Policyholders Xu Jia San and others, considering that after the second batch of relief funds of 20,000 yuan is distributed to the disaster-stricken policyholders (six yuan per household), there will still be a considerable surplus, intend to reallocate the surplus funds to charitable organizations to be used as funding for charitable causes and to aid the poor. They specifically sent a letter to the chairman of the Disaster Area Insurance Association yesterday to request approval. The original letter stated, "Respectfully submitted, I have been employed at Xiangmao Foreign Firm for many years. My original residence was at No. 02 and No. 404 on Baoshan Road, Zhabei. On August 27th of the Republic of China year, I purchased 1,000 taels of fire insurance, covering my property, from Shanghai United Fire & Marine Insurance, holding policy No. 52002. Subsequently, due to the outbreak of the January 28th War, my residence was unfortunately burned down on March 4th of that year. I repeatedly negotiated with the company for compensation without success. Fortunately, you generously provided relief by organizing the Zhabei Disaster Area Insurance Association to claim compensation on behalf of the distressed policyholders. After years, a relief fund of 40,000 yuan was finally allocated and, designated by the Bureau of Social Affairs, transferred to your association for distribution in two batches, six yuan per household, to show sympathy. I am deeply grateful. However, I already collected this relief fund during the first distribution. Seeing the crowds of disaster victims, I felt deeply saddened and unwilling to dispute its receipt. Considering that the harsh winter is approaching in an instant, the homeless and hungry are everywhere, crying out for food. Providing relief to those who are truly poor is something that cannot be delayed. Therefore, after much contemplation, I voluntarily donate the six yuan of fire insurance relief fund I am entitled to, to be used for Zhabei's charitable endeavors. This small amount is a drop in the bucket and insufficient to solve the problem, but it is merely intended as a first step. At the same time, I hope that other sympathetic individuals can embrace this intention. I appeal to your association to consider the suffering of the disaster victims in Zhabei with all remaining undistributed funds, and jointly donate to be uniformly used as funding for the more successful charitable organizations in Zhabei, so that the refugees can receive tangible benefits, not just for the good fortune of Zhabei... (omitted below)."

The Zikawei Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather around Shandong is cloudy and cold, with gradual improvement. The northwest breeze is turning from strong to gale force. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River have northwest to northeast winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River are overcast and cold, with possible snowfall. However, the weather is improving, with northwest to north winds. The East China Sea and Taiwan are overcast with rain, and the northeast monsoon is strengthening. The center of the second hurricane advanced to within about 120 miles of 17 degrees north latitude and 132 degrees east longitude at 6:00 AM, heading northeast. The Problem of Improving Chinese Musical Instruments (II)

— Ding Xielin

Secondly, those who have studied Western painting are mostly more able to appreciate Chinese painting, and those who have studied Western drama are mostly more able to appreciate Chinese drama. Assuming that music is an exception, those who have studied Western music cannot appreciate the monotonous Chinese music. However, can the monotony of Chinese music be blamed on Chinese instruments, especially the existing Chinese instruments that have not been improved with modern scientific knowledge? Moreover, only a very small number of intellectuals have received Western music education. What the general public can appreciate and play is Chinese music, and what they can buy and play with is Chinese musical instruments. Shop assistants who have finished a day's business, workers and farmers who have finished a day's hard work, and pedestrians who are tired, blow a xiao or play a erhu under the shade of a tree. This is a very common phenomenon, and it is a phenomenon worthy of admiration and encouragement. In a situation where we cannot persuade them to abandon the bamboo pipes or noisy bamboo buckets in their hands and replace them with an Italian violin, we can only improve the existing instruments in their hands and hope that the instruments will be played more widely after being improved. Furthermore, some people feel that the volume of most Chinese musical instruments is too small. It is okay for one person to play and listen alone, or for one person to play and a few people to listen, but it is completely useless in a large concert hall or when accompanying other instruments. The lack of loud instruments in China is indeed a big shortcoming. The volume of some Chinese musical instruments may not be increased or should not be increased, but the low volume itself is not necessarily a shortcoming. There are two aspects to volume: one is related to the music itself. Some pieces of music should use strong sounds, and some pieces of music should use soft sounds. Instruments with low volume are of course a style that should exist. The other aspect is related to the problem of sound transmission. It seems hopeless for thousands of people to listen to a guqin solo in a large concert hall. However, is it really hopeless? After the extreme progress of architectural acoustics, who can determine that even a Chinese guqin solo can change from a "barely audible sound in front of dozens of people" to a "barely audible sound in front of thousands of people"? Moreover, after the development of broadcasting technology, just for the sake of appreciating music, there may be no need to squeeze into a crowd of thousands of people at all.

What has been said above seems to be defending Chinese musical instruments everywhere, but it is absolutely not. What we are saying is only the abstract "Chinese musical instruments," not the various specific Chinese musical instruments that exist now. The instruments made and used by ordinary people now can be said to have many shortcomings in terms of structural principles. Taking the most common xiao and flute as an example, it can even be said that they are not musical instruments, because they lack the basic conditions of musical instruments, that is, they cannot produce tones that conform to the musical scale. We cannot agree with the views of the class of people who extremely worship Chinese inherent culture, and that is why. Now let us talk about this second view again. Regarding China's inherent musical culture, there are two aspects related to this article: the first is the musical scale. China has always linked the musical scale with the calendar and weights and measures, so dynasties have regarded it as a political system, and scholars have regarded it as a profound and specialized field of learning. There are probably more writings on the study and discussion of musical scales than writings on other aspects of music. However, it seems strange to say that in China's inherent musical culture, in addition to historical value, the most useless thing in seeking the progress of Chinese music in the future is the national heritage that belongs to the aspect of musical scales. This principle is easy to understand, that is because the musical scale has purely become science. Regarding this point, we may as well say a little more, because there are still many scholars who hope to find valuable things from piles of waste paper. We can divide the evolution of knowledge about musical scales into three stages. At first, we relied entirely on human hearing to recognize harmonious musical scales. There are two ways to obtain harmonious musical scales from musical instruments or any sound-emitting objects: one is to use pipes, and the other is to use strings. Greece discovered the method of seeking musical scales with strings in a very early era, and China discovered the method of seeking musical scales with pipes in an even earlier era, and these two methods are completely the same. They can all be named with the old Chinese name "the method of increasing and decreasing by thirds." The so-called method of increasing and decreasing by thirds is to increase the length of a pipe by one-third of its original length or decrease the length of a pipe by one-third of its original length. The new sound produced can be harmonious with the original sound. If we start with a pipe that is one foot long and continue to increase and decrease according to this method, we can obtain several pipes of different lengths that produce several sounds of different pitches. These sounds or musical scales are what are called "Huang Zhong," "Da Lu," etc. in Chinese books. This is the first stage. Decreasing by one-third results in a ratio of two to three, and increasing by one-third results in a ratio of three to four. Why can string lengths or pipe lengths that form simple ratios produce harmonious musical scales? This is the question raised by the great Greek philosopher Pythagoras.

Children's Education Novel

Little Boy (121)

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

When Mrs. Shu heard that this team of people was lost, a serious expression appeared on her face, so she sent Fu Lang to ride Tu Pi to find the little people back. When dinner was over, the whole family sat in the cool courtyard as usual, Fu Lang had already ridden Tu Pi back at a gallop, covered in dust, with a panicked expression on his face.

He shouted as soon as he was halfway through the gate passage, "Are they back?"

"No"! Saying this, Mrs. Shu jumped out of her chair. Her expression was so flustered that everyone jumped up and surrounded Fu Lang to listen to the news.

"I can't find them anywhere," he began to say; but before he could finish, a loud "Hello" made them all look up. In an instant, they were next to the house.

"Where are Nan En and Luo Bo?" Mrs. Shu shouted, grabbing Ai Mi with one hand. His strength made him think that his aunt had suddenly gone crazy.

"I don't know, they've gone home with other people. Aren't they back yet?" he quickly replied.

"No, Tai Fei and Tao Mo said they went with you."

"They didn't, and we didn't see them. We swam in the Ye Pond and then came back from the woods," said Jie Ke, who was very panicked.

"Call Mr. Pei, light the lights, and tell Manager Lai that I want him."

Finance Silver Market Showing Signs of Collapse, Standard Gold Price Continues to Rise by 8 Yuan 3 Jiao

Margin Increased Suddenly to Over 12,000 Pieces; Closing Price 50 Yuan, Buyers Still Outnumber Sellers by 26

The gold market yesterday continued to report sharp declines in foreign silver prices. Trading was even suspended in London. Prices stabilized upon opening, but due to large holders selling at high prices, they remained fluctuating. Reuters reported favorable news, and the silver market showed signs of collapse, with buying interest increasing. P>Practical Discussion on Organ Therapy for Lung Disease

— Physician Shen Xiangbo

There are indeed many internal medicines for treatment in modern times. Sweat cattle fill the beams. Fingers cannot be counted. However, in the practical experiment of clinical application, those who can achieve satisfactory results are rare. As for the medicines listed in the advertisements, although they are vigorously promoted for their efficacy, they are actually of no practical benefit. It is just a waste of harm. Sometimes it can stop coughs, but it is the power of the tranquilizers it contains, and it has no fundamental cure effect. Moreover, the ingredients in the internal medicines for lung disease have always been nothing more than calcium, phosphorus, fish liver oil, etc. This kind of medicine may only be effective for a while, or only suitable for the initial stage, or it will ruin the stomach if you take too much, or you cannot interrupt it if you take it for a long time. These are not fundamental medicines for treating diseases.

Recently, there is "Fei Huo" Phith Weal, which I consider to be the best internal medicine for tuberculosis. In the world, it can be called a unique effective medicine for treating lung. Fill in its defects. Harmonize and maintain its function. At the same time, a solid connective wall is built around the lesions to harden them. Promote the formation of scars. Completely wrap the evil demon's tuberculosis bacteria. Then let it self-destruct. Moreover, the effective components of this lung and spleen also have the power to promote blood coagulation. Therefore, "Fei Huo" Phith Weal's effect on preventing bleeding (hemoptysis) is particularly significant.

"Fei Huo" Phith Weal is mainly composed of lung and spleen organ components, and also contains lecithin (ie, lipids) and other nourishing and strengthening medicines. Therefore, after use, it can produce blood and fatty muscles, make physical strength vigorous, restore the gradually disappearing life functions, increase the natural resistance to diseases, and make patients leave the disease quickly and recover in a very short period of time. Taking "Fei Huo" Phith Weal can make the body healthy and strong, and increase the power to resist infection. Therefore, taking this medicine has the effect of "treating tuberculosis if you have tuberculosis", "increasing health and preventing tuberculosis if you don't have tuberculosis", which is suitable for both prevention and treatment.

Since I have been using "Fei Huo" Phith Weal in clinical practice, I have treated hundreds of cases of all stages of tuberculosis. All have unexpected results. Most of them are cured in one month for mild cases and no more than two or three months for severe cases. It is handy and the medicine cures the disease. It is indeed the champion of internal medicines for lung disease. The results of the application of this medicine are briefly described on the left.
