Publishing World

What is National Self-Confidence?

— Li Jianfang

"National Self-Confidence!" "National Self-Confidence!" The more people shout this slogan like crazy, the more this slogan loses its original meaning.

Some people say that national self-confidence is nothing more than belief in China's inherent morality; others say that promoting national self-confidence lies in knowing that we are a nation with thousands of years of history; still others say that promoting national self-confidence is about preserving the national essence and Chinese culture; and even more people say that promoting national self-confidence lies in our not forgetting our ancestors and worshiping them!

"National Self-Confidence," "National Self-Confidence," in the eyes of those who need this slogan to exercise their ability to deceive, it is simply the sculpture of the Greek Daedalus.

What exactly is national self-confidence?

To explain what national self-confidence is, one must first explain what personal self-confidence is. Is personal self-confidence like Ah Q, who, when someone grabs his queue and bumps his head against the wall four or five times, still mutters "Son beats father" in the spirit of "spiritual victory"? Of course not! Although personal self-confidence cannot lack a strong will and passion, a strong will and passion like Ah Q's definitely do not count as self-confidence. If one insists on saying that this is also a kind of self-confidence, then at most one can only say that it is a comical expression of self-confidence, and definitely cannot say that it is a solemn expression of self-confidence.

So, what is personal self-confidence? The most basic understanding of personal self-confidence should be a kind of confidence that an individual generates from reason and experience, from a deep understanding and grasp of their own abilities and the career they pursue. From this point of view, so-called national self-confidence is nothing more than a shared confidence that a nation generates from its own reason and experience, from a deep understanding and grasp of its own abilities and the great national goal it hopes for.

If this affirmation is correct, then not only promoting the restoration of old morality, promoting the preservation of national essence, promoting the preservation of Chinese culture, promoting idol worship, and promoting megalomania do not count as promoting national self-confidence, but also emptyly promoting the passion of loving the country and the nation without enlightening the people's intelligence and critical spirit also does not count as promoting national self-confidence. Why? Because the power of emotion cannot but be consistent with the rigor of logic. A passion that is not consistent with the rigor of logic, whether it comes from an individual or a nation, can at most explain a kind of respectable uselessness, a solemn childishness. The White Lotus Rebellion was not without a noble passion for loving the country and the race, but only because of their ignorance of their era, their movement, their sacrifices, not only did not benefit China, but instead deepened China's oppression and collapse.

Therefore, I say that national spirit or national self-confidence is definitely not a simple expression of national sentiment. It is rather a comprehensive expression of the people's deep understanding of their era and a deep grasp of their own abilities. National sentiment is indeed an important element of national self-confidence, but if national sentiment is not built on the inevitability of success, then so-called national sentiment will surely easily become yesterday's news!

Even in our daily lives, there are many things that, although they can deeply grab our hearts and make them suffer when starting from the emotional side, completely become meaningless things when starting from the rational side. Can one say that the things that give the strongest momentary stimulation to sentiment at the same time must have a deep practical significance for the life of the nation and the country?

From this, it can be known that an excessive emphasis on inherent morality, ethics, national essence, and even emotion, not only cannot guide the people's feelings and attention to understanding and researching actual phenomena to generate self-confidence, but also will guide them to the opposite direction, guiding them to directly oppose deep understanding and research, thus generating various paths of fantasy. The promotion of national self-confidence, to this point, cannot but become the promotion of national suicide!

From this perspective, only when national passion and national knowledge reach unity and consistency can a third thing be generated – national self-confidence, this is indeed definite and unshakable!

Based on this, it can be known that the various movements of restoration, reaction, and worshiping spirits currently advocated in China's ideological circles are not only not promoting national self-confidence, but simply eliminating national self-confidence from the root.

Wherever scientific interest and critical spirit gradually decrease, the individual's reason loses its power even more. Whenever the individuals' reason in a nation loses its power, they seek help from fantasy and the salvation of heroes, and thus lose national self-confidence. China first fell to the northern barbarians, not during the Spring and Autumn and Warring States period when knowledge was spreading, but during the Wei and Jin dynasties after Confucianism and Buddhism ruled China. The transformation of social relations was the cause, and the ideological cage and the tendency of the people at that time to seek help from transcendental mystical thought due to the ideological cage also greatly contributed to it!

In fact, any great historical movement or social movement is not only the result of conforming to the actual interests of the people or classes of that time, but also the result of a critical spirit, reason, and intellectual movement. The era when religious fantasy became the banner of historical movements has passed. Now, all liberation movements, especially the Chinese national liberation movement, if it cannot thoroughly have an intellectual and critical spirit liberation movement first to stimulate the intelligence and passion of the entire nation, then it is completely hopeless.

Having said this, I seem to no longer need to explain "What is national self-confidence." In conclusion, I only hope that readers must recognize one point: that is, those who, on the one hand, advocate restoration, advocate national essence, and advocate idol worship, and on the other hand, oppose new ideological movements, oppose the critical spirit, and oppose freedom of speech, are definitely not those who promote the power of national self-confidence. On the contrary, they are simply the grave diggers of the national liberation movement!

Chinese History Bibliography

— Ying Puhan

Compiled by Zheng Hesheng, Published by The Commercial Press

The history of our country is a record of the activities of our ancestors, and we all have a necessity to fully understand it. Without this knowledge, we cannot truly understand the position we are in today. However, to understand the past and comprehend the present, we must rely on a "general history." Mr. Liang Qichao, a historian of our country, once intended to compile a refined and complete "General History of China" "to serve as a reference for the activities of the general public in modern times." Unfortunately, most of his life was spent in officialdom, so this great plan was never realized. Needless to say, this is a great regret. Until now, we simply do not have a refined and complete history of our own country, so to understand the evolution of our nation, there is really no better way than to directly read the books of the history section.

However, the way to study lies first in finding a path; reading history is certainly no exception. Bibliography is the gateway to reading, and the bibliography of the history section is the gateway to reading history. This Chinese History Bibliography compiled by Mr. Zheng Hesheng is one of the good gateway books to reading the books of the Chinese history section.

The whole book is divided into ten chapters: (1) Origins of Ancient History, (2) Position of the History Section, (3) Origins and Development of the History Section, (4) Formal Records of the History Section, (5) Supplementary Records of the History Section, (6) Contemporary Records of the History Section, (7) On the Classification of the History Section, (8) Classification of Historical Materials, (9) On Historical Styles, (10) Conclusion. In the introductory examples, the compiler says, "The first chapter briefly describes the origins of historical books in our country, in order to rectify their foundation. The second and third chapters describe the position and origin of the history section, in order to generalize its essentials. The fourth, fifth, and sixth chapters describe the different categories of historical records, in order to glimpse their nuances. The formal records show their similarities, the supplementary records show their completeness, and the contemporary records show their changes. With these three aspects complete, the different categories can be generally understood. The seventh chapter describes the classifications of the history section by various scholars after Liu Zhiji, which have not been actually recorded, so it is called 'On'. ... The eighth and ninth chapters describe the classification of historical materials and historical styles, which briefly show the current scholars' division and combination of the history section, which is also a variation of the bibliography of the history section. The tenth chapter first describes the recording of the ancient people, in order to correct their errors, and then establishes a classification of the history section, in order to understand its origins." After reading, the reader can understand the general idea of the book.

The history of the bibliography of the history section in our country has been very long, such as the historical records of past dynasties and the Siku Quanshu Summary Catalogue and the Book List and Answers, all those who study history must practice recitation and understand them thoroughly. In addition to relying on the writings of previous scholars to make a systematic compilation, the compiler occasionally adds his own opinions and corrects them, or draws lessons from Europe and the West, completely changing the old habits, so there are many places of innovation. Now, please list a few of the most important points below to see the value of this book:

(1) Discernment of Gains and Losses—The item of False History is the most unreliable. Throughout the dynasties, catalogers of bibliography, either because of being confined to old theories or because of their circumstances, did not dare to openly criticize and correct them. In this book, the compiler distinguishes it under the item of False History in the Origins and Development of the History Section, saying: "False History records the history of false dynasties, which has the same meaning as Hegemonic History, and it does not matter who wrote it. The Siku Quanshu Summary Catalogue uses Later People's Records for the Chronicles and Self-written for False History, so the History of Yue and the Brief History of Korea are attached to the end. The names of Hegemonic and False are the most unreliable. Emphasizing the internal and belittling the external, although there is the righteousness of praise and blame in the Spring and Autumn Annals, respecting this and disparaging that actually loses the balance of the historian. Once the views of different customs are deeply rooted, the source of assimilation is difficult to discern. Moreover, each regards its own as correct, and all are the legitimate dynasty. 'Cao Wei refers to Wu and Shu as bandits, the Northern Dynasty refers to the Eastern Jin as usurpers, the South calls the North the Xuo Lu, and the North calls the South the Island Yi.' How can these be fair? However, those who were enemies at the time either wagged their tongues, and later generations should use history as a mirror and balance. They should not trace their prejudices and instruct later generations. Therefore, Ziyuan's theory of history only distinguishes between correct and miscellaneous, and does not say true or false. This shows that he is impartial, and success or failure is clearly revealed, without the need for praise or criticism. Once the host and guest are judged, good and evil are difficult to distinguish. Therefore, there is much to discuss about the category of false history."

(Pages 24) Also, the compiler corrects the Siku Quanshu Summary Catalogue, saying: "The Siku Quanshu Summary Catalogue, which came out later, has the most detailed classification regulations, but errors are also unavoidable. For the time being, let's take the old-style history item meanings as an example. For example, the Dongguan Hanji and the Later Han Shu of various families are not included in the official history in the old records, but the Summary Catalogue classifies them as separate histories. The category examples of separate histories say: 'The Dongguan Hanji and the supplementary remains of the Later Han Shu are all official histories; however, the books are incomplete, and they are not listed in the official history, so they are generally included in this category.' Also, the category examples of official history say: 'The books of annotations and explanations of various histories are all classified according to their categories. If Mao Guojin Jiang Zhiqi's Jin Shu deletes and modifies the original text, the Song Shi Xin Bian belongs to the books themselves. The Five Dynasties History Supplement and the Five Dynasties History Missing Texts are also added to the books themselves, and such examples are all included in separate histories.' Looking at the definition of separate history, it is a book that 'does not reach the official history and does not reach the miscellaneous history'. However, where is its boundary? The above-listed histories are originally in the form of biographies, but because the books are incomplete and are not listed in the official history, deleting and modifying the original text, adding to the books themselves, suddenly calling them separate histories, then what is the system? The classification standards are not consistent, so there are biographies in the hegemonic history. There are chronicles. There are records of events from beginning to end. Because it records the heroes, it is called the hegemonic history, and the rest of the miscellaneous histories and separate histories are similar. And among the biographies and chronicles, there are also books such as hegemonic history, miscellaneous history, and separate history. How can it be a standard for example categories?..." (Pages 234-235) Such discernment of gains and losses is evident everywhere in this book; only one example is prepared here, so it will not be listed further.

(2) The Compiler's Classification of the History Section—Whether it is the formal record, the supplementary record, or the contemporary record of the history section in our country. This is really due to the lack of scientific nature in the classification of academics in our country. Moreover, since recent times, geology, archeology, and other sciences have gradually developed, and the number of discovered underground physical historical materials has also increased. Thus, the scope of the history section has suddenly expanded. The re-compilation and amendment of the old history section catalog has become an urgent matter in academia. In view of this, the compiler of this book specifically took lessons from Europe and the West and established a "Classification of Future History Section Items" in the conclusion to show scholars. Its method divides history into three: "Historical Books", "Historical Compilations", and "Historical Objects". Historical books can be divided into two categories: Those that describe various events, integrating and interacting with each other are called "General History". General history can be divided into two categories: Those that take the era as the unit, such as the official histories and chronicles after the Historical Records. Those that take events as the standard, such as the Comprehensive Collection of Institutions, the Comprehensive Study of Documents, and the Histories of Events from Beginning to End. Those that describe a part of historical events, such as transportation, academics, customs, or art, are called "Special History". Such as the History of Chinese Transportation, the Song Wu Xue'an, the Ming Ru Xue'an, the Materials of Oriental Art, the History of Chinese Customs, etc. As for historical compilations, they can also be divided into three categories: Those that describe miscellaneous events without classified examples, such as the Classic of Mountains and Seas, the Discourses of the States, the Strategies of the Warring States, and magazines and newspapers, are called "Miscellaneous Records". Those that compile in order with clues to be found, such as various political essentials, meetings, and encyclopedias, are called "Collected Records". Those that have notes, supplements, textual research, explanations, tables, and records, which can supplement the deficiencies of the original history, such as the Historical Records Zhiyi, the Annotations of the History of the Three Kingdoms, etc., are called "Supplementations". As for artifacts, charts, specimens, and models, there is no difference in importance from historical books and historical compilations. However, they must take the era as the standard or take the region as the destination, then the outline is clear and the items are well-organized. The so-called taking the era as the standard, or taking the names of Tang, Yu, the Three Dynasties, Qin, and Han as the heading, and then listing in detail how many kinds of historical books, how many categories of historical compilations, and how many historical objects are in a certain era. Then, in the historical books, which is the general history and which is the special history; in the historical compilations, which is the miscellaneous record, which is the collected record, and which is the supplement; in the historical objects, which is the specimen, which is the model, and which is the chart. And then further cite which is the direct general history, which is the horizontal general history. In the special history, which is transportation, which is academics, etc. ... As for those who take the region as the destination, it is also the same, or by province, or by county ... it is all possible." (Pages 237-238) This classification method is outlined and tied, readers can understand it at a glance, it is truly the most concise of the historical section bibliographies of ancient and modern times.

In addition, the shrine bibliography of Sun Xingyan of the Qing Dynasty is often ignored by the world, but the compiler highly praises it, one is that "it really opens a precedent in bibliography, and it is proper in academics"; the other is that "it is simple and essential, sparse but not leaky." Indeed, Sun's bibliography can be unique and independent of the region, and it really has the value of being respected; and from this, we can also see the compiler's brilliant insight.

Culture Construction Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 3 Published

Culture Construction Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 3, is a special issue summarizing the past year. The contents include Qi Qisheng's China's Economy in the Past Year, Wu Yugan's China's Foreign Trade in the Past Year, Li Jianfang's China's Intellectual Circle in the Past Year, Wu Lifu's China's Literary Circle in the Past Year, Yang Ji's North China Newspapers in the Past Year, Liu Hanru's Highway Construction in the Past Year, Mi Baomin's China's Disasters in the Past Year, Wang Xinming's Domestic Affairs and Foreign Affairs in the Past Year, Zeng Jianping's International Politics in the Past Year, etc., depicting a simple outline of China's political, economic, intellectual, and cultural aspects in the past year. In addition, there are many specialized writings on monetary issues. The entire book has a total of two hundred pages, and the price remains the same, still selling for two jiao per copy.

Briefly Talk About Pictorials

— Yu Hui

Sixty to eighty percent of the materials in Chinese pictorials are cut from foreign pictorials, but Chinese pictorials are of a different type among the pictorials in the world.

When you walk into a bookstore, among the many books and magazines, the first to attract your attention must be those pictorials with bright colors. The covers of these pictorials are mostly printed with the charming photos of some movie stars and socialites of the time, or sensual nudes (please note the recent advertisement of a certain pictorial, their most important thing is the cover of a nude painting). This seems to be a regulation, and it is also sufficient to represent a certain trend in the publishing industry now.

We do not deny that pictorials are relatively leisure-oriented publications, but we cannot deny that pictorials are rich in propaganda and reporting functions. Pictorials report and instruct everything with figurative materials, so they are more clear and practical than abstract articles. Just because it requires readers to think deeply, just because it is easy to touch, figurative, so it can penetrate into all levels of society, and can have the greatest effect. He is invisibly taking on the task of subtle influence between readers without knowing it. In short, pictorials are an important publication.

The world's most famous pictorial in England is "Illustrated London News" (weekly), seeing its simple cover with a classical demeanor, you can know how different it is from Chinese pictorials. Here you can't find the charming photos of beauties, you can't see big feet and breasts, and each issue has an article on archeology, and the unearthed antiquities leave their figure here, the Royal Academy of Sciences, light, electricity, etc. inventions, and the introduction of customs and life in various places. Besides, you can also see a content that is full, but the writing is so relaxed, which is very commensurate with those pictures. Naturally, they are never stingy to spend many pages on the photos of major events at home and abroad. The American "New York Times Midweek Pictorial" (weekly) also has special features, just like the American personality. Here, the five colors are colorful, and attention is also paid to the new-style clothing and home furnishings, or the charming photos of a certain state queen, but the largest part is still the reports of current events at home and abroad and the introduction of scientific inventions. The French "Illustation" (weekly) is the same as the British "London Pictorial", without thighs and the like, most of the illustrations have detailed explanations, and the articles published are also rich in timeliness and interest. In addition, the German "Berliner Illiutrierte Zeitung" (weekly) after Hitler took power; each issue is full of photos of artillery, bombers, new-style submarines, and brave Nazi party members. The photos of the general assembly exercises are printed out with large sheets of paper. The above are all very famous pictorials, and what they have in common is the attention to current events at home and abroad. Each issue is very fresh. When King Alexander of Yugoslavia and Foreign Minister Barthou of France were killed in Marseille, a week later, the American and British pictorials had photos of the time, even a glimpse before the killing. They often buy photos at a great price. And the reason why most of them are weeklies (the world's famous pictorials can be said to be all weeklies), I think it is nothing more than the reason for emphasizing the timeliness of the photos.

But Chinese pictorials, in contrast, are quite disappointing to us. Just a little attention to their covers, which are the most attractive to readers, is given to some beauties, and you can see the attitude and intention of the pictorial editors. Some even use his own characteristics to publish comparisons between pig lungs and human buttocks, portraits of high-achieving students of a certain school (in addition, there are some boring literary works), etc., taking the vulgar as interesting, and taking the boring as serious, and emphasizing nude paintings and the shadows of celebrities and socialites, although it is said to be adapted to the needs of readers, but we can't help but admit that the formation of this interest in the reader layer has a close relationship with these magazines. Today, when you walk into a young man's room, nine out of ten people must have films of some movie stars or mermaids posted or hung on their desks. Chinese youth still have this problem and this mood in this difficult environment. Today's pictorial editors cannot shirk their responsibility. As for what kind of attitude the pictorial should take, I have mentioned it briefly above. In short, if we don't focus on enlightenment and reporting, I would rather the Chinese publishing industry have no pictorials.

What is the relationship? On the eve of the opening of the National Goods Promotion Team, I would like to suspend this meaning to pray for its success.

Promote National Goods and the Industrial Revolution

— Qiao Yunsu

Last month, the Ministry of Finance promulgated an order to abolish the silver dollar and implement legal currency. This is a major change in the history of Chinese finance. On the one hand, the government is preventing the outflow of northern silver, but on the other hand, it is because the commercial, economic, and rural economies have become extremely withered. It resolutely used the new currency to revive and adjust the exhausted financial state of the country. According to bankers, currency inflation is actually because countries are trying to buy silver endlessly. Our traitorous merchants, thinking that great profit is in it, do not hesitate to damage the vitality of the national economy and desperately help the perpetrators. In this way, according to the opinions of the majority of people, national products can easily become active, and at the very least, there is hope that the number of imports and exports can be balanced. This is a great help to the promotion of national goods that has been promoted by the government for many years, and we are very fortunate for the future of the national economy. However, on the other hand, we need to know that promoting national goods is a movement that should be paid attention to in many aspects. For example, everyone has shown sincerity in using national goods, but there are no excellent national products to replace them, or perhaps the goods can be compared with foreign goods, but the price is extremely expensive, or even certain foreign goods are flooding the market, but there is no invention equivalent to a certain foreign goods, and the price is extremely expensive. It is not the intention of national goods merchants to deliberately raise the price, or be implicated by the blood capital! Or be hampered by manufacturing technology! Everywhere is a major obstacle to promoting national goods. Speaking of this, we have to speculate on the phrase "industrial revolution"; there is such a paragraph on the People's Livelihood Principle ... If it is a society where industry is not yet developed, then on the one hand, develop national capital, important production and public utilities belong to the public, then encourage private enterprises, protect private capital under the original state of capitalist socialization, so that the industry develops towards the path of industrial revolution! ... These few words, of course, refer to the rough branches and abandoned them. To solve the maze of important production undertakings, I have to distort it a bit. Roughly "improve production" and "reduce prices" can also be attached to the banner of the "industrial revolution", right? Now, those who need to engage in production undertakings also need to move towards the path of revolution. How to improve the excellent products so that they can compete with foreign goods, and how to reduce the price to ease the burden of users. I recently felt that two school supplies are really not clever. One is wax paper, which has a trend that foreign goods must be used. Among the national products, there are those with a price of three yuan per tube, which can be printed to less than one or twenty sheets, and the skylight is opened, and it cannot be printed again. The other is chalk, which, as soon as it reaches the blackboard, breaks into pieces, losing money and wasting time! It is even more necessary to reduce the enthusiasm of users. Although this cannot represent the general national wax paper chalk, the two kinds that I have received are not blatantly proclaiming the only national product - we want to solve these problems, we should hope for the industrial revolution, and the tools of the industrial revolution must be included in "science" - because only science - is the general key to saving the country.

The Achievement of the Women's National Products Year

— Tian Xu Wo Sheng

The Shen Bao National Products Weekly published on November 18th of the 24th year contained a report from the National Products Trade Bureau: In the past ten months of this year, the value of imported foreign perfumes and cosmetics totaled 356,318 customs gold units, equivalent to 634,313 national currency units, a figure considered alarming. However, compared to the previous year, it has indeed decreased by more than half, which cannot be denied as an achievement of the Women's National Products Year. Reading the 71st issue of "National Products New Sound" published by the Joint Association on January 15th of this year, it stated that from January to November of the 23rd year, the value of imported foreign perfumes and cosmetics totaled 818,640 customs gold units, equivalent to 1,580,898 national currency units. Averaging over eleven months, the monthly outflow of money was over 143,400 yuan. This year, the ten-month average is only over 63,400 yuan, a reduction to 44%, indicating that among every 100 people, 56 no longer use foreign goods. Generally, changes in customs originate from the concepts of public preference and aversion. Since more than half of the people no longer use foreign goods, it is certain that more than half of the people prefer to use domestic goods. The small number of people who still use foreign goods mostly do so because they are too infatuated with Europeanization and have always been accustomed to using luxury goods, feeling that domestic goods cannot compare. Therefore, they have no choice but to abandon domestic goods and choose foreign goods. This is similar to eating rice; those who are accustomed to eating first-class machine-polished japonica rice will not be forced to eat brown rice, even if it is given to them for free. Therefore, I believe that the most important key to recovering outflowing profits lies in the products of domestic goods factories. Focusing solely on cutting corners and reducing materials and competing on price is a misconception. The proverb "cheap goods are not good, and good goods are not cheap" is indeed an accurate and unshakeable common principle. A rice store that only sells inferior or second-class rice instead of first-class rice, even if it uses cheap prices to attract customers in the market, will definitely not attract wealthy households to buy. This can be stated with certainty. Some say that the decrease of more than half in imported cosmetics is due to reduced purchasing power. However, taking the example of the Family Industrial Cooperative, this year's decrease compared to last year is only 10%, while imported goods have decreased to 44%, indicating that it is not due to purchasing power. However, in the future, almost all imported goods will increase in price by more than 20%, and domestic goods will also inevitably increase in price. The two will inevitably show a clear example of one growing and the other declining. Next year, it may be possible to change the trade balance from import surplus to export surplus, which is not necessarily impossible.

The Welcome and Introduction of the "China Oil Lamp"

— Xiao Shi

In large cities, electric lights provide illumination all night, while in the rural areas of the interior, kerosene lamps are still popular. Not to mention that electric lights are not easy to install, even if there are electric lights, poor farmers cannot afford to enjoy this bright happiness. Villagers call kerosene lamps "foreign lamps" because they come from abroad. The burning kerosene is called "foreign oil" because it is also an imported product. If every household in the country uses one foreign lamp on average—and there are actually more than that number—then more than 100 million lamps are needed. The loss from foreign lamps is still limited, but the loss from foreign oil every day is truly incalculable.

Now there is good news: exquisite and practical China oil lamps have appeared. A month ago, I saw a news item in the newspaper about someone inventing a China oil lamp, and the day before yesterday, I saw proof of the fact at a friend's house, which made me extremely happy. This oil lamp is a product of the Shanghai China Oil Lamp Company, with the "Bagua" (Eight Trigrams) brand trademark, and is entirely a domestic product. The burning material is not kerosene, not foreign oil, but soybean oil, rapeseed oil, and peanut oil, which are readily available in rural areas. The light it emits is brighter than that of foreign lamps, and the style, whether as a table lamp or a hanging lamp, is also extremely beautiful. The bulb is even more clean and bright, which I truly admire and makes me happy. I am confident that in the near future, this Bagua China oil lamp will become popular throughout the country. In my opinion, its advantages also include the following:

Using a China lamp and burning China oil, especially raw materials inherent in rural areas, not only is the price cheaper than foreign oil, but it can also reduce a huge loss; advantage one. Since it is called kerosene, it naturally has kerosene gas. If the fire is not extinguished after sleeping, there will be black gas in the nose in the morning. People who do not enjoy the happiness of electric lights have this experience. Now, switching to soybean oil can avoid this problem. If rapeseed oil is burned, it will even have the effect of improving eyesight; advantage two. Kerosene gas is most harmful to the human body, especially to the lungs. For people with lung diseases, it is simply adding insult to injury. Soybean oil and rapeseed oil are ordinary foods, and not only have no kerosene gas, but also have no smoke; advantage three. Kerosene catches fire easily, and fires caused by kerosene lamps being knocked over occur everywhere. Soybean oil does not have this disadvantage; advantage four.

Since the Bagua brand China oil lamp has all these advantages, how can it not be welcomed and happily introduced? Some people often lament that Chinese people love to use foreign goods. In fact, Chinese people are not unpatriotic and do not dislike using Chinese goods. As long as there are suitable substitutes, they will naturally be loved and used. Taking this lamp as an example, everyone agrees with it. I have introduced this lamp to many farmers, and after they have seen the actual proof, no one does not agree with and happily use it. Everyone wants to ask me to buy one for them, and everyone also says that the Chinese are longer suffering than before. It can be seen that patriotism is an innate conscience. From this perspective, the future of China is very promising.

Medical Lecture

Proper Treatment of Gonorrhea

— Physician Yuan Yimin

Gonorrhea is a difficult-to-treat condition. This is undeniable by anyone. The reason for its difficulty in treatment is partly due to the difficulty in completely eradicating the gonococcus, and also partly due to the patient's failure to strictly adhere to a regimen of health preservation. Moreover, sometimes it is due to incomplete treatment, etc., all of which are sufficient to prolong the disease and progress to a chronic stage. At this point, the disease has spread to other areas. If treatment is not properly managed, the hope of a permanent cure is lost. At this time, the gonococcus is often deeply hidden in the mucous membrane. Outwardly, there are no subjective symptoms whatsoever. Even the patient himself does not feel much discomfort. However, every time the body is overworked or excessively drinks alcohol, it is sufficient to recur. In the past, the treatment of gonorrhea was limited to internal medicine, washing, and injection. In recent years, the progress of medicine has been remarkable. Such as the injection of pigments and mixed vaccines, the strong internal use of membrane-permeable bactericidal agent "Mesaltropin," shortwave diathermy and the latest turbid treatment machine, as well as the injection of local gonorrhea serum "Gonoserol," etc. All these are excellent. The efficacy is superior to all treatments. It is indeed the most appropriate method for treating gonorrhea. However, this method must be performed by experienced specialists. so that the dosage and condition can be accurately judged. For example, the Chunzai Hospital at No. 66 French Concession in this city employs many physicians. Women's examinations are assisted by female doctors. Electrotherapy equipment is fully available. Its equipment is complete, and its treatment is appropriate. For the time being, no other hospital can be compared to it.

The Composition of Opium and Its Physiological Effects

— Physician She Lei

The unripe poppy capsule is cut open with a knife, and the fluid that flows out is taken and allowed to dry to form opium. The main plant salt in it is morphine. In addition to morphine, opium also contains papaverine, codeine, narcotine, thebaine, etc., totaling eighteen kinds of alkaloids. Among them, the first three are all related to morphine. Although thebaine is chemically close to morphine, its medicinal properties suggest that it should be classified under the strychnine group.

The main component of opium is morphine. Morphine is a phenanthrene derivative that can paralyze the brain. In particular, reflex movements caused by pain are also paralyzed. Therefore, medical practitioners unanimously recognize it as an effective analgesic and constantly use it to achieve the purpose of pain relief. However, after the application of morphine, the reflex excitability of the spinal cord is enhanced. In certain animals, it can cause rigidity, just like strychnine. The results of experiments by Japanese scholar Kenzo Tamura showed that the reason for such rigidity is the crystalline nitromorphine produced in the body by the acidification of morphine, or the amorphous substance produced by its acidification. Its effect is similar to a mixture of strychnine and picrotoxin. If this convulsive poison is further acidified, it loses its toxicity, and acidification is especially rapid in warm-blooded animals. Therefore, the phenomenon of convulsions is rarely seen. However, convulsions can occur if a large amount of nitromorphine is administered or injected into the subarachnoid space. Other anesthetics, such as papaverine, codeine, and narcotine, have weaker anesthetic effects than morphine.

Choosing Stomach Medicine

— (Physician Ma Fangweng)

The usual symptoms of stomach diseases are nausea, vomiting, acid reflux, heartburn, stomach pain, and abdominal distension. Those who suffer from this disease not only hinder diet and nutrition, but also suffer greatly from nerve damage. If left untreated, the stomach wall will ulcerate, which may lead to gastric ulcer. Examining suitable drugs for these symptoms, none is better than alkaline agents. Among alkaline preparations, the most outstanding and superior is "Wei Bao." "Wei Bao" has various medicinal effects that exceed ordinary preparations, which are briefly described below. (1) Regular use is harmless. (2) It has a particularly strong analgesic and antiemetic effect. (3) It promotes digestion and regulates the physiological functions of the stomach. (4) It can neutralize stomach acid and absorb harmful substances in the stomach and intestines. (5) It is fragrant and palatable, making it easy to take. With such excellent effects, it is more than worthy of being praised as a sacred medicine for stomach diseases. This medicine costs two yuan per box and is sold at Ren Shou Western Pharmacy, No. 1 Laodehang Lane, Mintini Yin Road, Baxianqiao, French Concession, this city.

Questions and Answers about Diseases

— Editor

This magazine has opened this column. Any questions about diseases can be sent by letter for inquiry. We will be responsible for providing specific answers. Please briefly explain the illness and treatment process in the letter and send it to the Fubian Department, Shanghai Post Office Box 1668. If you do not want it to be disclosed in this magazine and require a written reply, please attach a return postage of two cents for local mail and five cents for out-of-town mail.

Answer: There are various causes of dysmenorrhea. If you only seek the purpose of pain relief, then any pain reliever can be effective. Common Symptoms of Sexual Neurasthenia

— Physician Feng Shanliang

Sexual neurasthenia is originally a partial phenomenon of neurasthenia. It is named because it is specifically manifested in the genital area. However, its various common symptoms are also found in various parts of the body, not only in the genital area. Usually seen are insomnia, but its type is different. It may be a clear obstacle to falling asleep, or it may be the inability to sleep soundly and easy waking. The stimulation of the five senses is high, so there are often symptoms of hypersensitivity. In addition to pain, the head also has a feeling of heaviness and discomfort. Dizziness is felt after overwork and drinking. There is occasional belching and vomiting. The digestive system suffers from nervous indigestion. Constipation and diarrhea occur alternately. Patients are becoming increasingly thin, and the muscles are also loose. Fatigue is easily felt after work. This is a characteristic of this disease. Moreover, discomfort and weakness are very clear, so willpower is weak, mental concentration is difficult, and thinking and memory are reduced. Mental abilities are markedly impaired. If forced to engage in labor, the aforementioned ailments will increase significantly, and may even become a mental illness. However, the aforementioned ailments are part of the general symptoms of neurasthenia. In sexual neurasthenia, of course, diseases of the genital area are especially severe. I have already mentioned it before, so I will not repeat it here. In the past, this disease was only treated with drugs, and the effects were generally slow. In recent times, with the prevalence of electrical therapy, this disease has finally had the hope of a definite and rapid cure. Among electrical therapies, shortwave diathermy is especially good. As for drugs, organ therapy is quite valuable. Other drugs, such as egg yolk lecithin, organic phosphorus compounds, and aphrodisiacs, are also highly appreciated. Over-the-counter medicines such as Arolsen have been clinically used and have been quite effective. (Arolsen) is sold at Ren Shou Western Pharmacy, No. 1 Laodehang Lane, Mintini Yin Road, Baxianqiao, French Concession, this city. Each box costs one yuan and fifty cents. (Editor)

Talk

Student Parade Petition in Peiping

— Li Min

Students from fifteen public and private universities, including Peiping University in Beiping, gathered in front of Zhongnanhai Qianmen at 10 a.m. on the ninth of this month. Together they went to Jurentang to petition He Yingqin, opposing any facts that would divide national unity, demanding unity for national salvation, and safeguarding the integrity of the country. Immediately they lined up and paraded through the streets. There were more than a thousand students. In addition, there were five or six hundred students from Yenching and Tsinghua Universities outside Xicheng, but they were unable to enter the city because Xizhimen was closed by the police. This is the first student petition movement heard in the two or three years since the Shanghai Truce Agreement. According to reports, the Peiping authorities, fearing that it would cause "Sino-foreign disputes," have strictly instructed the principals of various schools to "take the initiative to guide and stop the students, maintain order, and not be incited. If there is any unruly behavior, the government will never tolerate it." We suddenly heard about the petition of students in Peiping, and it truly feels like Ding Lingwei returned as a crane, with a sense of "the scenery is the same, but people are different." Another generation has passed in the world, and one does not know where the tears should come from!

Recently, North China has been in turmoil with the so-called "autonomy issue." Some time ago, Tianjin saw the discovery of strange names such as "North China Anti-Communist Security Commander" and "People's Self-Defense Dare-to-Die Corps." This is clearly an act of rebellion against the country, and it would be most appropriate to apply the Emergency Criminal Law for Endangering the Republic of China. However, it did not encounter any obstruction, and it was only when the truly genuine people tore up their banners that the matter came to an end. This time, the purpose of the Peiping student parade was to safeguard national sovereignty. Fortunately, the police intervention was limited to using batons to drive them away. Otherwise, if any trouble were to arise, it would be another unfortunate event.

Not long ago, the Central Daily News published an editorial stating that today's news censorship policy is extremely unreasonable. The country is in such a critical state, but the general public is still kept in the dark, which may be the result of the current unreasonable news censorship policy. This article was widely circulated among the general public. As a result, some people very much hope that the central government can reform the current news censorship policy. On the one hand, for the still un-dead popular sentiment, they also hope that the central government can connect with it and use it as a strong backing for diplomacy. This hope is indeed something that every member of the public desperately wants to see realized. Today's parade and petition of Peiping students can at least be said to be an expression of a part of the popular sentiment. This is completely different from the autonomy movement and the People's Self-Defense Dare-to-Die Corps, etc., initiated by another part of the so-called people in North China. I believe that the general public is holding a full of enthusiasm and sincerely hoping that the government can accept this precious gift.

Older Sister

— Ying Guangjun

Just thinking of my older sister fills me with immense unease. My older sister is currently trapped in a difficult situation, but I cannot help her to get out of her predicament sooner. Yet, when we were young, she helped us, her younger siblings, with so many things.

Speaking of my older sister, she was practically my second mother. At that time, our family was living the life of a large family. The women had to take turns cooking. The family farmed the land and hired monthly and yearly laborers. A lot of food had to be cooked. As soon as my mother went to work, my older sister became our mother. She took care of us with the utmost care. My younger sister would sometimes cry and fuss, which would irritate even me, but my older sister calmly took care of her. If it hadn't been for my older sister at that time, I really don't know

Page 18

what we would have done. And my older brother, who was also four years younger than my older sister, would often quarrel with her. My older sister was only fifteen years old, but she was very capable of being a little mother.

In the evening, my mother would send us to bed and often say to us:

"Without your older sister, you wouldn't have been able to live to be so old. When you grow up, don't forget your older sister's kindness. Only then will you not fail to live up to her deep affection for you."

Yes, I still remember these words clearly to this day. I am sorry that I only remember my older sister's kindness, but I have not repaid even a bit of her deep affection for taking care of us back then. I am so sorry to my older sister.

When my older sister was sixteen years old, she learned to make shoes for us. My older brother and I would run around outside all day long, wearing out our shoes very quickly. My older sister had to make shoes for us every six or seven days. She would jokingly say to us:

"You two need to wear two pairs of iron shoes."

She also helped my mother make most of our clothes. If my mother didn't have such a virtuous and capable helper, she definitely wouldn't have been able to manage.

My older sister is a capable older sister, a good older sister, so whenever someone came to propose marriage, I would always oppose the matchmaker. At worst, I would scold them a few times, and at worst, I would hit them with a broom. Once, Grandpa Hu Er came to propose marriage, and I poured a bucket of water over his head. I even jumped up and down and shouted:

"You bad egg, get out! My older sister doesn't need you to be a matchmaker."

I begged my mother not to let my older sister marry and to keep her at home until she was old. She treats us so well that we can't bear to let her leave. But my mother wouldn't agree, and she couldn't explain why either. She just said that all girls have to get married when they grow up. We felt that my mother's words were too unfair to my older sister. My older sister helped her with so many things, but she was willing to marry her off.

We asked my older sister if she wanted to get married. My older sister always blushed and didn't say anything. When we pressed her, she would say:

"Older sister won't leave. Older sister can't bear to leave you."

After we told my mother this news, we mocked her:

"Mom, what do you say? Older sister herself said that she doesn't want to get married. Don't talk to the matchmaker about my older sister's marriage anymore."

Fortunately, because the families that the matchmakers proposed several times were not very suitable, my older sister's marriage was never settled. This went on until she was twenty-seven years old. By this time, we realized the mistake of keeping her from marrying before. We were also worried about her marriage and hoped that it could be settled as soon as possible.

But my older sister seemed to grow older day by day, and she rarely smiled on her face. But her love for us was still the same as before. During this time, because I was studying outside, I was not often at home every year. Once we met, we seemed particularly close. Remembering the old days, I often laughed unconsciously and teased my older sister:

"Now I won't keep you anymore. I even hope that more matchmakers will come."

In the winter of that year, when she was twenty-seven years old, Hu Er was still the matchmaker who settled my older sister's marriage. Because of her age, she didn't even get to enjoy the rights of a first marriage and was married to someone as a concubine. After she went there, she lived peacefully for more than two years. My older sister even gave birth to a daughter. Although she unfortunately died young, it didn't diminish her indifference to life. She was able to settle into her position and do her work.

Last summer, I received a letter from her saying that her husband was about to marry another woman. There was no reason given, probably because he was tired of the old and loved the new. She asked me to help her think of a solution, and she even said heartbreaking words, saying that she regretted getting married and that she had to suffer another torment in this world.

What can I do? Unless I go back and discuss it in person, but I don't want to return to my smog-filled hometown. Her predicament has therefore been delayed until today without being resolved. I am so sorry to my older sister.

Skinning a Dead Ox

— Chen Liang

It was like joyful news of opening a granary for relief; when old man Shunfu's sick ox died, the illusion of smelling the aroma of beef aroused the heightened appetite of everyone. However, this was a perverse desire. That ox was more likely to have died of old age rather than sickness; and more likely to have died of exhaustion rather than old age. From the mouth of old man Shunfu, who was getting old with a head of gray hair, a pair of worried old eyes, and always clear snot under his nostrils, I learned the brief history of that dead ox.

Six years ago, old man Shunfu still had a mill, specializing in grinding flour, corn, soybeans, and many other grains for the people in the village. The family relied on the milling fees paid by people to make a living. Every day, every day, he put that ox on the millstone, dragging the large stone disc of two or three hundred catties, pacing incessantly. If it stopped even slightly, the crisp, stinging sound of a rattan whip would fall on its thin body. When the new wheat was harvested, until the end of the year, the mill was grinding grain for people all day and night without stopping. For the sake of life, old man Shunfu had to endure the hardship and had to spur his ox. The ox, for the sake of a little straw to fill its stomach and a little water, had to run spitting white foam, suffering the poisonous whip.

During a summer epidemic, old man Shunfu's seventeen-year-old son died of illness while grazing the ox outside. He mourned this son and arranged a grand funeral for him like an adult. The money was borrowed from Grandpa Shubo. However, the years deteriorated year by year, and he could not afford to repay the principal and interest. At the end of the year, the millstone was taken away to offset the debt. From then on, the mill was idle, old man Shunfu was idle, and the ox was also idle. However, this idleness caused by debt was precisely forming the panic that he and it had no means of support for their lives.

Food for the old couple, food for the ox. Where to get it? Where to get it? That heavy stone millstone, although old man Shunfu's family shed a lot of sweat for it, although the ox put in a lot of effort for it, it was always a kind of life, a kind of coexisting life! Finally, when sowing wheat last year, he pleaded again and again to the township director, the clan elder, and several large landowners, asking them to give him a little of the village's fields to cultivate. Thus, the lives of old man Shunfu and his old ox, which had worked hard for several years, were tightly bound to that plow again, pouring sweat into the hard yellow soil. Old man Shunfu, who was climbing back onto the line of life, still thought it was a gift of happiness, right? However, happiness and life are incompatible like ice and charcoal!

Old man Shunfu's ox finally fell ill, collapsed in the idle mill, staring with moist eyes, its belly pressed down, and it wouldn't eat even if straw was thrown to its mouth. The ox doctor walked up to it, shook his head, and left. One day, two days... it almost became a large specimen of an ox skeleton, and died.

"Alas, the ox is dead. I don't know when our two old bones will..." the old woman shrank in the corner of the mill, sighing old man Shunfu.

The young men skinning the dead ox were busy with all their might, with seven hands and eight feet, their hands stained with purplish-black blood, splattered on several small sharp knives. The bones and skin were collected by old man Shunfu to sell for money, and the meat was divided among everyone. Families who were stingy with firewood and seasonings didn't want any. My uncle also cut off a large piece and stewed it in an earthenware pot, adding fennel and soy sauce. When it was almost cooked, the whole house was filled with an enticing aroma that heightened the appetite. He told me to go to bed later to eat beef, but I politely declined. He thought I didn't eat dead beef for hygiene reasons. He explained that he added ginger and sugar to the pot. In the end, I still didn't taste it. I couldn't forget the sighing sentence:

"Alas, the ox is dead. I don't know when our two old bones will..."

Chen Wu's Soul is "Passed Down"

"The Imperial Envoy is scheduled to continue performing for five days at the Central Grand Theater from the 20th to the 24th of this month.

A Spring "Dream" Under the "Peach Blossom" Tree

Shanghai Company's Domestic Ice Hong Lin

The most interesting thing in life is dreaming. All romantic miracles, things that are impossible in the real world, can be done in the land of dreams.

The American film "A Night of Love" released in Shanghai last year, the young man played by Eddie Cantor, after being driven out of the Roman exhibition hall, wandered alone on the street, and was suddenly caught by the guards in the ancient Roman city. So he began all sorts of strange encounters: he was sometimes dragged to the auction house and sold as a slave; sometimes he was loved by the queen; sometimes he was in the palace full of pink and greasy fragrance and beautiful women like clouds, surrounded by porridge-like daughters; sometimes he was imprisoned in a gloomy and miserable hell... He experienced all the encounters in life, and the result was originally a big dream.

Shanghai Film Company's new work "Peach Blossom Dream," directed by Du Yu, is a song and dance film that has the same flavor as "A Night of Love." There is a large group of girls in that film, all of whom are poor girls who sell flowers and newspapers on the street, or wash clothes for others. They work hard every day and play together. Because of a chance encounter, they visited the magnificent song and dance performances of the rich, and everyone was tempted by a little superficial vanity. The most beautiful girl among them (played by Yin Mingzhu) went to the stream to wash clothes, sat under the peach blossom forest, and fell into a trance. She gradually fell into a dream. So this poor laundry girl suddenly became a popular song and dance queen, bossing around, wealthy and glorious, invincible, falling in love and enjoying herself, doing everything. But she fell into an irredeemable tragic situation, and woke up from the dream sadly. The housewife who was washing and mending was standing in front of her with angry eyes...

The world of dreams is the most beautiful and romantic. "Peach Blossom Dream" is the world of all absurd and romantic imaginations.

Suzhou Film Studio

Stimulating Shots in "Hero of the Hour"

A Collection of News Regarding the "New Style Drama Society"

Mr. Wei Wei, the director of "National Duty," has come to Suzhou from Shanghai and has hired several new spoken drama actors, rehearsing on schedule every day.

The stage for the rehearsal of "National Duty" has been set up in the factory's photography studio, resembling a small theater in shape.

In the third act of "National Duty," there is a tense crowd scene, featuring a model of a giant ship. The art department has begun its construction, and its grand and lifelike appearance is quite similar to the final scene of "Roar, China!"

Mr. You Zhou, the playwright of the factory, has completed a screenplay titled "Stealing Noodles" and is currently preparing the procedures for initial and final review. It is planned that this screenplay will be one of the two projects to begin filming after "Miss Suzhou."

During the spare time from rehearsing "National Duty," they are actively training in Mandarin and rehearsing several world-renowned one-act plays, which are listed below:

"Roar," directed by Mr. Wei Wei, performed by the entire cast.

"The Rising of the Bright Moon," directed by Mr. Chen Shouqiu, performed by Wang Jing, You Zhou, and others.

"Thief," namely Sinclair's "The Man Who Lived Upstairs," directed by Wang Jing, starring Hong Ying.

"Song of the Pomegranate," written and directed by Mr. Dan, with music and songs composed by Mr. Yang Tianxi, is purely a one-act song, dance, and music drama, performed by young Gu Min and famous singers from Suzhou and Shanghai.

"Lady Sima," written and directed by Mr. You Zhou, performed by Han Yan, Hong Ying, Gu Min, Zhang Hong, and others.
